1932.05.21

The Question of Soldiers Not Participating in Civil War 1

The September 18th Incident suddenly erupted, allowing the confrontational situation between Nanjing and Guangdong to ease through a so-called unified and peaceful conference, achieving temporary harmony. However, the competition for power and the conflicts of interest between them remained constant. Especially constrained by the adverse diplomatic situation and domestic public opinion, they only engaged in covert struggles, actively brewing chaos while waiting for an opportunity to strike. They initially dared not immediately turn to open conflict. Now that the Sino-Japanese armistice in Shanghai has just been agreed upon, signs of internal strife are becoming increasingly clear. The situation in Guangdong is suddenly tense. The issue of reorganizing the naval and air forces on the surface has already led to a serious situation. Currently, the navy has become independent, and Chen Jitang of Guangzhou will issue a clear order to suppress it. The outbreak of civil strife seems inevitable again. Another group of soldiers is again clamoring not to participate in internal warfare, hoping to win the favor of the people. Although it seems reasonable on the surface, examining its content reveals that everyone has their own background and position. However, for the past twenty years, except for the brief period of the Northern Expedition of the National Revolutionary Army from 1926 to the short-lived unification, a glimmer of dawn, warlords have risen and fallen, and wars have continued one after another. This recurring historical tragedy truly makes us heartbroken and unable to do anything but weep blood to the sky. Therefore, today, hearing the call for soldiers to no longer participate in civil war, regardless of whether it is true or false, our people view it as precious and pleasing, expressing deep sympathy. However, we believe that today, to fundamentally eliminate civil war, the solution does not lie in the passive "non-participation," nor in the superficial propaganda of "non-participation." Over the past twenty years of recurring wars, who does not have a pretext to borrow? Furthermore, who does not say that war is out of sheer necessity? The so-called "unbearable" and "wiping away tears to brandish weapons" have become stereotypical pronouncements. In this situation, there is no right or wrong, no truth or falsehood. It has become a chaotic situation of warlord infighting, which will not end simply because a portion of people do not participate. Moreover, the propaganda of not participating in civil war is obviously a kind of tactic. They are unwilling to sacrifice their positions, unwilling to give up their rights, each possessing strong troops, each establishing their own factions. The army is an individual's army, and the benefits are for oneself. When the desire for power is ignited internally and imperialists tempt them externally, even if they want to avoid war, it is impossible. The so-called non-participation in civil war is merely a pretext to deceive people. Therefore, we should understand the causes and consequences of the tense situation in Guangdong today, where swords are drawn and bows are strung. We should also not be overly pleased with the propaganda of no longer participating in civil war. The crux of the problem lies elsewhere, not here. Unless the warlord system is overthrown, there is no way to end internal strife.

Our attitude towards the non-war proposition was already determined in a previous commentary, "Guangdong's Domestic Non-War Movement." If soldiers today truly have a great epiphany and realize the mistakes of the past, then the way to save the country no longer lies in the passive non-participation in civil war.

The Takeover Committee Held a Joint Meeting Yesterday 2

To Determine Takeover Procedures for the Day After Tomorrow

Personnel to be Sent Today to Inspect First

Japanese Side Notifies of Continued Troop Withdrawal

Regarding the handover of the area north of the Zhabei Railway and the Zhenru area, the Japanese side has decided to hand it over to us for takeover on the 23rd. Therefore, the Takeover Committee specially convened a joint meeting yesterday with all relevant parties to discuss the takeover method. The committee also decided to send personnel to Zhabei this morning for inspection and to discuss the takeover procedures with the Japanese side. Yesterday, the Japanese members of the Joint Committee officially notified the Chairman of the Joint Committee, Cunningham, and our members, Yu Wen and Wen Yingxing, that they had decided to withdraw the Japanese troops from Yangxing on the 24th. At the same time, the Shizilin Fort, the Paotaiwan Barracks, and the Sanguantang Ammunition Depot will be handed over to us for takeover. The Takeover Committee has already assigned personnel to be responsible for the takeover. The details are recorded as follows:

Yesterday's Takeover Meeting 3

At 10:30 a.m. yesterday, the Takeover Committee convened a joint meeting to discuss the method of taking over the area north of the Zhabei Railway (i.e., the jurisdictional scope of the Fourth District, Fifth District, and the Second Branch of the Fifth District). Those present yesterday included Yin Rugeng, Li Shengjun, Tao Xiaojie, Cha Nanqiang, Gong Xikui of the Public Security Bureau, Yin Tixin, Huang Ming, He Yiming, Niu Jingjian, Lei Xianbai of the Public Utilities Bureau, Zhong Shijie of the Education Bureau, Jing Song of the Land Bureau, Xue Cixin and Zhou Zanbang of the Public Works Bureau, Sun Yongyi of the Social Affairs Bureau, Liang Encheng of the Finance Bureau, He Bingsong of the Commercial Press, Wang Bincan of the Zhabei Defense Corps, Dong Zhihe of the Fire Brigade, Zeng Zhihong, Jin Zhu, and Li Zhaoyu of the South Road Bureau, Hong Jingping of the Shanghai-Taicang Long-Distance Bus Company, Zheng Chengqing of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Shen Mingpan and Xu Tiepu of the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company, and Tao Fengshan of the Telegraph Bureau. First, Chairman Yin Rugeng reported, stating that the committee is scheduled to take over the area north of the Zhabei Railway, formerly under the jurisdiction of the Fourth District, Fifth District, and the Second Branch of the Fifth District, at 2:00 p.m. on the 23rd. The area extends east to the Yokohama River and the Songhu Railway, and southwest and north to Liuying Road, with the railway as the boundary on two sides. It has been agreed that the Japanese side will send personnel to discuss and inspect tomorrow (i.e., today) before the actual takeover, and to arrange everything. Today, a joint meeting is specially convened to discuss the takeover method. After Yin's report, everyone present decided that at 8:00 a.m. this morning, the Public Security and Public Utilities groups will go to Zhabei for inspection separately. The Public Security group will be responsible for discussing defense handover matters, and all public security and fire protection issues will be handled by the group. The Public Utilities group will be responsible for all administrative affairs related to water, electricity, transportation, telephone, street lights, and various municipal bureaus. They will gather and depart from the Lianshe at 8:00 a.m. today. The personnel for this task have been assigned. The Public Security group includes four members of the Takeover Committee: Special Commissioners Li Shengjun, Tao Xiaojie, and Cha Nanqiang; nine members of the Public Security Bureau: Huang Ming, Gong Xikui, Yin Tixin, He Yiming, Wu Shaolin, Niu Jingjian, Xia Qingyu, Lin Cishan, and Bao Ju; one member of the Defense Corps: Wang Binyan; and three members of the Fire Brigade: Dong Zhihe, Chen Yousheng, and Liang Huimin. The Public Utilities group includes two members of the Public Utilities Bureau: Zheng Hecheng and Sun Kaizhi; one member of the Education Bureau: Zhong Shijie; two members of the Public Works Bureau: Zhou Zanbang and Xue Cixin; one member of the Finance Bureau: Liang Encheng; one member of the Technical and Health Bureau: Jiang Shicheng. Representatives from the Two Roads Bureau and the Commercial Press will be appointed by the meeting itself to go there. The Two Roads Bureau also plans to inspect everything in the Zhenru area today.

The Takeover of Miaohang Announcement 4

The Takeover Committee issued a statement yesterday regarding the takeover of Miaohang the day before yesterday, stating that at 7:00 p.m. on May 19, the personnel who took over Miaohang were Lu Fengpu, the second district chief of Baoshan County, Liu Guiting, the second branch chief of the Baoshan County Public Security Bureau, and Zhu Huang, the third squadron leader of the Capital Security Team. The Japanese troops in Miaohang had withdrawn four or five days earlier, and the Japanese side did not notify our side or the Joint Committee. Upon receiving the news, the committee was concerned that public security problems might arise in the area, and sent personnel to take over the area on the afternoon of the 19th. According to reports from the takeover personnel Lu Fengpu and others, Lu and Liu arrived in Dachang at 4:00 p.m., met with Squadron Leader Zhu Huang, and led a security team of 20 people, arriving in Miaohang at around 6:00 p.m. Because the houses in the town were all destroyed or occupied by refugees, making it impossible to station police, they were stationed at the Zhan Rice Mill in Zhancun, about half a mile west of the town. The area is still relatively peaceful.

Notification of Continued Withdrawal 5

Okazaki Katsuo, the Japanese member of the Joint Committee (replacing Murai), officially notified Cunningham, the chairman of the Joint Committee, and our members Yu Hongjun and Wen Yingxing yesterday that they had decided to completely withdraw the Japanese troops from Yangxing, Shizilin Fort, Paotaiwan Barracks, and the Sanguantang Ammunition Depot at 11:00 a.m. on the 23rd of this month. They informed our side to discuss the matter in advance so that the handover could be completed as scheduled. Regarding this matter, our Takeover Committee has already properly assigned receiving personnel to each location. Shi Ze will be responsible for taking over Shizilin Fort, Cao Jinbai will take over Paotaiwan Barracks, and Song Lichen will be responsible for taking over the Sanguantang Ammunition Depot. In addition, Liu Shouyu, Lin Tong, and Liu Xikang Renchu will assist in taking over the above-mentioned agencies.

Sending Personnel to Inspect Zhabei 6

The Japanese troops stationed west of Songhu Road and north of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway in Zhabei are scheduled to withdraw on the 23rd. The Takeover Committee convened a meeting yesterday to plan the takeover. It was decided that personnel would be sent to inspect the Zhabei area first at 8:00 a.m. today and to discuss with the Japanese authorities in advance to make arrangements. According to investigations by the Hua Dong News Agency, the Japanese troops in Zhabei are scheduled to withdraw on the 23rd. However, in other locations, west of Songhu Road and south of the Yokohama River and Liuying Road, a portion of the area cannot be withdrawn immediately. The area accounts for approximately two-tenths of the entire Zhabei area.

Central Government Sends Personnel to Investigate 7

The Propaganda Committee of the Central Party Headquarters believes that since Shanghai has fallen and suffered severely from burning and killing, and a takeover is imminent, everything in the disaster area should be investigated clearly. Therefore, it sent Huang Ying, the director-general of the committee, and others to Shanghai to be responsible for investigating everything in the takeover area and the initial state of the takeover. Huang and others arrived in Shanghai yesterday and will go to various districts to inspect and take photos for propaganda purposes.

The Truth About the Japanese Handing Over Soldiers and Civilians 8

No Soldiers Were Captured During Combat

Civilians Were All Innocently Abducted

When our side took over Jiangwan on the 19th, we also received a total of 39 of our captured soldiers and civilians. The details were recorded in yesterday's newspaper. It is still necessary to record the situation at the time of the takeover and the truth about the capture of our soldiers. The following is a supplementary account of the findings of the investigation: On that day, Shen Yi, the secretary of the 19th Route Army's Shanghai Office, accompanied Zhan Baoguang, the staff officer of the headquarters, and representatives from the municipal government, went to the North Station. The Japanese staff officer Tomita received them, handed over 39 prisoners and a roster, and asked Staff Officer Zhan to take them back. He said that these were all prisoners of your army. He said this with a smile, as if to show the attitude of a victor. Zhan replied that perhaps there were civilians mixed in and that names should be called to distinguish them. Tomita said that they were all your countrymen and that they should be taken back together. Zhan firmly refused and finally ordered the prisoners to line up and call out their names one by one. Then he asked the soldiers of the 19th Army and the 5th Army to step forward three steps. At that time, ten soldiers of the 19th Army stepped forward, and six soldiers of the 5th Army stepped forward. The rest remained still. Then Zhan said to Tomita, "These sixteen are our captured soldiers, and the remaining twenty-three are civilians." Then he led them to the reception center. These were the details of the handover of prisoners the day before yesterday. As for the truth about how the soldiers were captured, according to the soldiers, they were either hospitalized in the rear hospital in Nanxiang, or wounded on the front line, and were captured when the troops were withdrawn. According to the Wounded Soldiers Management Committee, these soldiers still need to be sent to the Red Cross Hospital for treatment. From this, it can be seen that no one was captured during combat on the front line, and the civilians were all innocently abducted. The Japanese forced them to admit that they were plainclothes or new recruits. According to the captured soldiers and civilians, they were treated very harshly after being captured. The Japanese soldiers forced the soldiers to reveal our military secrets and beat them severely. The daily meals consisted of only two bowls of white porridge for breakfast and a rice ball for dinner.

The Devastation of Miaohang After the Calamity 9

Piles of Rubble, Traces of Battle Still Barely Discernible

Although the Cannons Have Ceased, the Loyal Sons Still Flow with Green Blood

Jin Mu's House, covering three hundred mu, the east end of Toutang Street, and the west end of Xitang Street, all in the vicinity of Miaohang Township, were the most fiercely fought areas during the war. Because the reporter of the New Voice News Agency learned that the Japanese army had withdrawn on the 18th and that our security team had also been stationed there, he specially drove to the area yesterday afternoon to see the real situation. The scene after the calamity was desolate and infinitely sad. The details are recorded as follows:

A Glimpse Along the Way 10

At 1:00 p.m., turning north from the Zhabei Railway, we proceeded along Zhongshan Road. At the intersection with the railway, we first passed through a Japanese army post for inspection. After that, there were no major obstacles. There were still many pedestrians coming and going on Zhongshan Road. Then we proceeded south along the Shanghai-Taicang Road. The Japanese sentries had disappeared. However, there were more than 20 instances of telephone poles lying on the ground on both sides, seemingly sawn off by someone. When we arrived at Baohua Temple, the car could no longer proceed because the road ahead was narrow and we could only walk. So we abandoned the car and walked, and temporarily found a villager to lead the way. After about half a mile, we saw a chicken and duck company with about 20 or so houses, quite large in scale, now all destroyed by artillery fire. Only a small house at the rear end remains intact. Slightly to the northwest is the Hou Residence, all the houses of which have been reduced to rubble. According to the villagers, the destruction of the Hou Residence was caused by arson by the Japanese afterwards, which was also tragic. Along the way, we saw trenches about four or five miles long, most of which had been plowed and leveled by farmers, but the remaining traces were still faintly discernible. After proceeding for about four miles, we arrived at the Zhan Residence, which used to be the headquarters of a certain brigade of our Fifth Army. The houses have not been damaged much. Behind the back door of a press in the east, there is a communication trench leading directly to Miaohang, about three miles long, which has now been mostly filled in. After walking for another half an hour, we finally arrived at Miaohang.

The Tragic Situation in Miaohang 11

The village of Miaohang has a total of 65 households, and the houses are all built along the Goose Creek. Fortunately, more than a dozen low houses and thatched huts in the west were not hit by artillery fire, and the villagers have also moved back. South of the creek is a small school called Goose Creek Elementary School, which used to have more than 50 students, two classrooms, and two teachers. The school affairs were quite developed in a small village. After this war disaster, the interior is empty, and the surrounding walls are dangerous. Only an outline remains, and the traces of bullets are as dense as a honeycomb. A dozen steps from the school is the Zhou Residence, which has been reduced to ashes. Next to it is the Wang Residence, which has a total of 34 houses, going straight to the Sicao Temple at the back. Now, however, all that can be seen is a pile of rubble, which has become a scorched earth. At that time, we met a Wang woman who had suffered. According to her, there were a total of five families with the same surname, with more than 20 houses, who were engaged in the oil pressing industry (i.e., pressing oil for others). During the previous emergency, they rushed out in a hurry, first to Luodian, and then fled east and west, passing through more than 20 places in the middle, experiencing all kinds of hardships and displacement. They finally arrived in Shanghai after many twists and turns. Now, the family is scattered, and she is alone. She only returned to her hometown a week ago to see it. However, the houses have been completely destroyed, with not a single tile to cover her body. The household goods have been lost without a trace. In a hurry, she tried to hire someone to build a small shack, which was only enough to accommodate her. Eating, drinking, and living are all done while sitting on the ground. Moreover, three family members died in the fire, one of whom was already 70 years old. As she spoke, tears welled up in her eyes. The tragic state of her life truly made us unable to bear to hear it. The Sicao Temple (the name of Miaohang comes from this) on the southeast bank of the Wang Residence was the place where the two sides fought fiercely. The temple has a total of three rooms and three courtyards, and the villagers were very devout in worshiping and burning incense. Since the outbreak of the war, the temple has been the stronghold of our front line. Large trenches were built all around, and there are also traces of trenches along the east wall of the temple. The idols such as the Great Lord and the Third Lord have all had their hands and feet broken and are lying on the ground. When our army retreated, it was occupied by the Japanese army. The first squadron of the 9th Engineering Brigade of the Kanazawa Engineering Corps was stationed in the temple. When the Japanese army was stationed there, they broke a hole in the roof, supported it with three bamboo poles, and hung a Japanese flag on the top, which still exists. It is truly regrettable to see the enemy flag flaunting its power within our territory. There is an open space next to it. According to reports, when our army retreated, many of the dead were left behind and were burned and destroyed by the Japanese. Now, only black traces remain, left for us to mourn. About thirty steps from here is the Three Heroes' Tomb, which the Japanese often boast about. It is said that the Japanese army must visit this place every day to pray, rain or shine. I wonder what the Chinese people will think of the national soul in front of the Dachang Shanghai-Taicang Railway Station when they see this. About four miles east of the temple is Jin Mu's House, which was also the most fiercely fought battlefield at the time. Slightly to the north are East Tang Street and West Tang Street. Less than 20% of the houses in Jin Mu's House remain. East and West Tang Streets were completely destroyed by fire. Although the residents have returned one after another, they are only temporarily setting up temporary shelters. Three miles south of Miaohang is Sanbai Mu Tou, which used to be farmland. Later, a capitalist from Shanghai invested in purchasing 300 mu of land to build more than 40 houses, planning to build a new village there and open up roads that could lead to Shanghai. After this war, huge trenches, about four miles long, and newly built houses were the most severely damaged. At that time, blood filled the ditches and corpses were everywhere. Looking at it from a distance, it was almost like the fallen rice in the autumn harvest. The sight of it made us sad.

Our Police are Stationed 12

The Japanese army stationed there numbered only a hundred or so people, and they all suddenly withdrew on the 18th. At that time, our side immediately sent Wang Liansheng, the platoon leader of the third squadron of the first battalion of the Capital Security Team, along with 15 policemen, from Dachang. Because there was no way to station in Miaohang, they were temporarily stationed in the Zhan Residence. The area is now extremely peaceful. From yesterday onwards, they began to investigate the population.

Notice to Pacify the People 13

Bian Yushan, the commander of the Capital Security Team, issued a notice to pacify the people, which read: "In view of the withdrawal of the Japanese army and the fact that this department has been ordered to take over the defense, all maintenance measures have been properly planned. All farmers, workers, and merchants should return to their homes as soon as possible and diligently pursue their occupations so as to restore the original state as soon as possible. However, after the war disaster, there may be unscrupulous villains, and there may be weapons left behind. It is not permissible to hide them privately. Please report to this department quickly, and rewards and punishments will be given separately. This is a sincere announcement. Please abide by it and do not forget."

The Japanese Army Still Comes 14

After the Japanese army withdrew, they still came to inspect the area in groups of three or five on the day before yesterday and yesterday, and to pray at the Three Heroes' Tomb. At the same time, they completely removed the markers erected at the places where the remaining Japanese soldiers were buried. They did not come after 5:00 p.m.

Which Troops are Stationed in Southern Songjiang? 15

Various Groups and National Salvation Associations Telegraphed Wang Jingwei and Chiang Kai-shek to Inquire

The Shanghai Various Groups and National Salvation Joint Association held its 50th Executive Council meeting at 3:00 p.m. yesterday. Yin Zhiling, Li Cishan, Chu Huiseng, Chen Peide, Chen Yafu, Shen Zurun, Huang Renzhi, Wang Aoxi, and others attended. Chu Huiseng was elected as chairman, and Shen Binfu took the minutes. The resolutions of the meeting were as follows: (1) Chen Peide and others responded to the assignment to investigate the case of Yongyuan Company purchasing Japanese goods and matches, stating that there was no evidence. The meeting decided to reply to the company with a slight warning. (2) Hu Zushun reported that the National Salvation Joint Association of Various Groups in Beiping was established on the 15th and resolved four important cases, as well as the situation of Japanese soldiers provoking trouble in Beiping for days. The meeting decided to reply by letter. (3) The Telegraph Workers' National Salvation Association stated that the Japanese intend to establish a free city in Shanghai and have obtained the support of various countries. Some Shanghai celebrities and landowners have also echoed this proposal. The meeting decided that according to the erroneous talk in today's newspaper about the British Overseas Association advocating a round table conference, the association should issue a declaration firmly opposing it and send letters to the Chinese Taxpayers' Association, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the General Labor Union, the Citizens' Association, the Bankers' Association, the Local Maintenance Association, the various Road Business Associations, the Lawyers' Association, etc., to unite in strong opposition. (4) On the issue of troops stationed in Southern Songjiang and Pudong, the meeting decided to telegraph the Executive Yuan and the Military Affairs Commission to inquire about the situation and appointed Wang Aoxi to draft the telegram. The meeting adjourned at around 6:00 p.m. The text of the telegram is recorded below: Urgent, Nanjing Executive Yuan Director Wang and Military Affairs Commission Chairman Chiang, Since the signing of the armistice agreement, the Japanese side has widely spread the rumor that our side has acknowledged that troops will no longer be stationed in Southern Songjiang and Pudong. At that time, Director Wang and Foreign Minister Luo successively issued responsible statements denying this. This association also deeply believes this is not true. However, the armistice meeting record published in the Shanghai Evening Post on the 12th of this month clearly states that troops will not be stationed in Southern Songjiang and Pudong. Several days have passed, and the authorities have not denied this. The people of Shanghai are extremely alarmed. Recently, the Shanghai Garrison Headquarters has moved back to its office, and newspapers have reported that the headquarters is guarded by police. This is bizarre and shocking. Members were specially sent to Longhua to investigate yesterday and confirmed that the police were guarding the headquarters and that no troops were stationed there. However, according to Chief of Staff Zhang of the Garrison Headquarters, as reported today, the headquarters has requested troops from the Ministry of Military Affairs and will be stationed in Southern Songjiang soon. We are delighted to hear this. However, the public security of Shanghai needs to be maintained urgently. Which troops will the government send to Shanghai, and when will they arrive? We sincerely hope that you will send a telegram in advance to dispel the doubts of the people. This association will inform the public and prepare to welcome them.

Shirakawa's Condition Suddenly Worsens 16

Japan Sends Miki Ryoei to Shanghai for Examination

Tokyo, 20th (Far East News Agency) - General Shirakawa, commander-in-chief of the Japanese army in Shanghai, who was injured in the Hongkou Park bombing on April 29, and Lieutenant General Ueda, commander of the 9th Division, who was also injured, were treated by doctors in the Army Garrison Hospital. Yesterday, General Shirakawa suddenly passed bloody stool. Doctors diagnosed that it was caused by a sudden illness in the internal organs. They were quite alarmed. When the Japanese Consulate General in Shanghai heard about it, they were very worried and telegraphed back to Japan immediately. Therefore, the Ministry of the Army plans to send another doctor to Shanghai in the near future to treat Shirakawa's illness.

Tokyo, 20th (Dentsu News Agency) - The Ministry of the Army has sent Miki Ryoei, a medical doctor, first-class army medical officer, and chief of internal medicine at the Military Medical School, to Shanghai overnight to perform surgery on General Shirakawa. Miki is scheduled to depart from Tokyo Station tonight due to the sudden deterioration of General Shirakawa's condition.

Within the Concession 17

The Issue of Japanese Military Activities

The Municipal Council Lodges a Strong Protest - At the Municipal Council meeting on the 18th of this month, the chairman reported that, according to the authority granted by the previous meeting, and because of certain incidents involving Japanese armed forces in the concession, which had been confirmed by the Chief of Police, he had sent a formal protest to the Consular Body, requesting the Consular Body to make efforts to persuade the Japanese naval and land forces not to interfere with or obstruct the activities of the Municipal Council's police and other personnel. As of this moment, the Consular Body has not replied. The content and wording of the letter have been severely criticized by the Japanese newspapers, but the Municipal Council's strong protest against the incident was unavoidable.

The Japanese Army Continues to Withdraw 18

The 18th Infantry Brigade of the 9th Infantry Division of the Japanese Army, which was originally stationed in Jiangwan, Dachang, Miaohang, etc., is now gradually withdrawing and heading to Wusong and Yangshupu to board ships and return home. The headquarters officers and men of the 18th Brigade and the Akazawa unit of the 19th Regiment have all received departure orders. They are scheduled to board the Kairyu Maru, Kaian Maru, Noe Maru, and other ships sent by the Ministry of the Army in Wusong and Yangshupu today to return home. Yesterday, Kono Koukichi, the commander of the 18th Brigade, bid farewell to the Japanese community groups and the Chamber of Commerce in Hongkou. The troops are scheduled to leave Shanghai and return to Japan this afternoon.

Engineers 19

The 9th Engineer Battalion attached to the 9th Division, divided into three companies, had its first company arrive at the Dalian Wharf in Yangshupu yesterday morning to collect all its supplies. The supplies, which were many, were also transported by trucks to the wharf and loaded into the Guang'an Maru transport ship. At the same time, the 2nd Infantry Battalion of the 36th Regiment also boarded the Guang'an Maru to return to their country. The battalion's ammunition and military supplies were also loaded onto the ship, which departed from Wusong at 11:30 a.m. When the battalion departed, a warship was sent by the navy to escort it.

Tokyo, 20th (Dentsu News Agency) - The Japanese naval authorities have ordered Vice Admiral Nomura, commander of the 3rd Fleet, Rear Admiral Shimada, chief of staff, and Rear Admiral Shiozawa, commander of the 1st Overseas Fleet, to go to Tokyo around June 10. Commander Shiozawa will become the director of the Education Bureau or the director of the Military Affairs Bureau. His successor will be Rear Admiral Sakano, who was appointed as an attaché to the 3rd Fleet today.

Counting and Sealing Up Japanese Goods Begins from the Day Before Yesterday 20

People's Organizations Joint Association Puts Forward Six Suggestions

Investigation of Confiscated Goods Committee Work 21

The city's Pre-War of Resistance Confiscated Goods Investigation Committee is jointly organized by representatives from the Municipal Government, Public Security Bureau, Social Affairs Bureau, Municipal Party Headquarters, Local Court, Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Lawyers Association, Accountants Association, and the Pre-War of Resistance Association, etc. It has already held several meetings and has decided to start inventorying the Japanese goods sealed in various warehouses starting from the day before yesterday. It is said that the inventory procedures are very complicated and will take about a week to complete.

Opinions of Public Organizations 22

A letter from the Federation of Public Organizations to the Confiscated Goods Clearance Committee states: (Title omitted) According to reports, your committee has taken over the anti-Japanese confiscated goods and started clearance. It is known that where great profit lies, evil abounds, especially in these recent times when people's hearts are not as they used to be and morality is declining. This is an unavoidable fact. The decline of all personality, reputation, and morality originates from this. Since the September 18th Incident, Shanghai has accumulated the achievements of the struggle of anti-Japanese members from all walks of life, resulting in the confiscation of various enemy goods, which demonstrates the spirit of our national history and deters those foreign powers who plot against us. However, due to the huge value and quantity of these goods, all kinds of treacherous merchants, corrupt officials, and local scoundrels have been coveting them for a long time, plotting to divide the spoils. Now that the humiliating agreement has been made and the government has declared great success, our people still maintain their consistent opposition. Anti-Japanese work absolutely cannot be stopped, and clearing the confiscated goods is premature, which is apparently the government's hidden intention to end the anti-Japanese movement, appease the enemy, and use the goods for private gain. This is done with lightning speed, secretly and unexpectedly, causing widespread concern. How can we not be outraged? Our association, representing all the people of Shanghai, respectfully submits the following opinions: (1) Regarding the organization, canceling the confiscation of goods has been reported by the Japanese media and recorded in the meeting minutes, which has also been repeatedly denied by diplomatic authorities. Now, it is being carried out in great haste. We are deeply concerned that it may be clearance in name but disposal in reality. Who will believe that it is not to fulfill the agreement and understanding? However, the officials of the authorities are skilled at covering things up. They call it clearance and invite representatives from various organizations to participate, but these so-called representatives are already eager to curry favor. Is this batch of confiscated goods to be monopolized by a few committee members? This is a question that all of Shanghai should pay attention to, and it is also a question that you should carefully consider. If it starts in the name of anti-Japanese resistance but ends with suspicions of making a fortune, what will the world say? Even filial sons and obedient grandsons will not be able to conceal it. If you must take the step of temporarily suspending the process, you should expand the organization and convene another meeting, taking the opinions of the majority of genuine anti-Japanese organizations in Shanghai as the standard. Otherwise, it will absolutely not be effective. (2) Continue the inspection of confiscated goods. This is the only way to genuinely resist for the long term. What the brutal Japanese deeply hate and detest is what our country is determined to uphold to the death. War can be stopped, but confiscation of goods cannot be stopped. If confiscation of goods stops, it will not only mean the loss of the country but also the loss of the race. It is still possible to carry out clearance today, but the clearance organization must be thorough and transparent, and the timing must be appropriate. It should only be carried out when absolutely necessary. While clearing the old goods, we should also inspect new goods. Only by doing both can we demonstrate the uprightness and integrity of our race. Moreover, only by thoroughly implementing the work of continued inspection can we wash away the shame of the collapse of the anti-Japanese confiscated goods solution. If your committee is ordered to carry out only clearance and from now on takes fundamental measures to eliminate the problem, then you will not be able to escape the title of traitor, and where will your dignity and integrity be? Rather than taking office, it is better to resign and let the authorities act recklessly and handle the matter directly. As for the distribution and use of the confiscated goods after clearance, it should be based on the principles of anti-Japanese resistance, as follows: (1) Promote domestic goods, (2) Provide relief to the unemployed, (3) Assist righteous troops, and (4) Comfort disaster victims. Any other measures that are seemingly for the public good but are ambiguous and not closely related to the principles of anti-Japanese resistance should be absolutely excluded. Recently, rumors have spread that a certain minister is coming to Shanghai to negotiate and allocate a certain amount of funds for a certain project. Although this is unfounded speculation, it is still chilling. As your committee has just taken office, and you are all known for your integrity, we hope that you will adopt the opinions of the public and provide the people of Shanghai with the opportunity to participate in public discussions in the shortest possible time, and at the same time clarify the future anti-Japanese and national salvation policy. With collective wisdom and efforts, we can continue to strive forward. Then your committee and your intentions can be clarified, and the future of the anti-Japanese resistance will be very fortunate. Our association feels a sense of crisis and dares not remain silent. In addition to notifying all the people of Shanghai and all the anti-Japanese and national salvation organizations, we hereby send this letter and hope that you will consider and respond. (Below omitted) Sincerely, The Shanghai Federation of Public Organizations.

Railway Bureau Reorganizes Railway Property 23

Railway Police Gather at Upper South Station to Await Transfer

Due to the impending withdrawal of Japanese troops from the North Station, the Engineering Department of the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway Bureau dispatched 60 laborers to the North Station and the area around Macgregor Road yesterday morning to repair the tracks. The railway property inside the station needs to be guarded by personnel urgently. Therefore, the Railway Bureau, with the approval of the Japanese military authorities, specially dispatched 12 railway police officers yesterday to protect the North Station and the railway property in various places to prevent theft. After the withdrawal of the Japanese troops, methods will be devised to resume traffic.

Yesterday morning, the Traffic Department dispatched important officials to inspect the North Station and the area around Macgregor Road along the route.

After receiving news of the withdrawal of Japanese troops, Rong Yi, the chief of the two railway police sections, immediately began preparing for the defense of the two railways when traffic resumes. Since the Shanghai-Kunshan section was occupied by the Japanese and the lines were destroyed, the passes are not easily accessible. Without a strong police force, it would be difficult to discuss the matter. Therefore, a comprehensive plan was made to transfer well-trained senior police officers from the Hangzhou-Nanjing, Changzhou, Zhenjiang, and Wuxi police sections, either six or seven, or ten, all of whom are required to gather at the Upper South Station before the 20th to await transfer. The senior police officers have all complied with the order and gathered at Upper South Station, totaling more than 50 people. It is said that after the North Station is taken over, armed senior police officers will be stationed at each station from Shanghai to Suzhou for protection. Officers and police officers from the First and Second Nanjing sections will be responsible, and dozens of student police officers will be dispatched to assist. After traffic resumes, each passenger train will be assigned one investigator, leading one police chief and six police officers to travel back and forth for protection. The senior police officers accompanying the trains will be filled by the well-trained senior police officers transferred from each section, in order to ensure thoroughness and safety for travelers.

Sun Ke's Recent Statement 24

Claims He Will Not Go to Nanjing Until His Proposals Can Be Implemented

Says He Had No Prior Knowledge of the Opening of Japanese Goods Issue

The New Voice Agency reports: Yesterday, due to news reports that Sun Ke had agreed to go to Nanjing to attend the Third Plenary Session of the Central Committee to be convened in June, the reporter visited Mr. Sun at his residence on Molier Road at 10 a.m. Mr. Sun received the reporter in his study. The reporter asked: (1) Today's newspaper reported that you have agreed to go to Nanjing to attend the Third Plenary Session of the Central Committee to be convened in June. Is this true? Sun replied: Recently, various Chinese and Western newspapers have reported news of my going to Nanjing almost every day. I don't know where these reports come from. My resignation last time was not accidental, and I have no personal grievances with the current central officials in charge. The difference lies in our views on domestic and foreign policies. The principles I published the other day are all practical proposals based on facts, not just empty slogans to cater to social psychology. The country's situation has become so dangerous. How can those with political responsibility engage in selfish power struggles? As for my going to Nanjing, I believe that as long as it benefits the country, I will not hesitate to brave danger. However, I will not go to Nanjing until my proposals can be implemented. (2) Did Chen Mingshu and Tan Zhen visit you in Shanghai the other day? Sun replied: Chen and Tan both visited me, but they only discussed the principles and content of the proposals and did not mention any other issues. (3) It is rumored that Chen Gongbo came to Shanghai this time with two missions: one is to represent the government and welcome you to Nanjing, and the other is to secretly carry out the opening of the confiscated enemy goods in Shanghai last year. According to the Beijing dispatch in the newspaper on the 19th, Chen reported to the Executive Yuan meeting the details of his talks with you in Shanghai. Can you tell us the details of your talks? Sun replied: I not only did not know his mission this time, but I have not even met him. The rumors that Chen came to Shanghai to see me and the details of our meeting are all untrue. (4) It is said that Chen was already opening up Japanese goods when you were the President of the Executive Yuan. Did you ever agree to it at that time? Sun replied: I absolutely had no prior knowledge of this matter. (5) It is said that this case has been discussed in the political conference several times, but it has not been passed due to opposition. If the government eventually sells Japanese goods, what will be your attitude? Sun replied: I think this matter is of great importance, and the government will not violate public opinion and implement it blindly. (6) What is the inside story of the reorganization of the Guangdong Air Force and Navy? Sun replied: I did not ask about this matter at first. Recently, I heard that Mr. Hu is mediating, and I think it will not be a problem. At this point, due to the arrival of other guests, the reporter excused himself and left.

League of Nations Investigation Team Halts Trip to Heilongjiang 25

Lytton and His Entourage Scheduled to Depart from Harbin for Shenyang This Morning

Ten Commissioners to Travel to Heilongjiang by Plane for Inspection

(Harbin) The Lytton Investigation Team has canceled its planned trip to Qiqihar tomorrow morning due to the presence of anti-Manchukuo forces along the western section of the China Eastern Railway, fearing for their safety. However, the team can still obtain information from the area. Ten experts from the team will travel to Qiqihar by plane from Harbin to investigate the situation there. The Investigation Team is scheduled to return to Shenyang on Saturday and Sunday.

(Reuters dispatch, 20th)

(Harbin) Lord Lytton's secretary and Mr. Fujii and his entourage of eight people are scheduled to travel to Qiqihar by plane at 10:00 tomorrow morning. Lord Lytton and the other members of the Investigation Team will depart from here for Shenyang at 8:00 tomorrow morning. (Dentsu dispatch, 20th)

Developing Towards Western Heilongjiang 26

Occupying the Entire Area Between Longjiang and Mangou

Battles in the Songpu Area Underway

(Harbin) It was recently reported here that the entire area from Qiqihar to Mangou has been occupied by Ma Zhanshan. However, the main force of Ma's army is still in the Keshan and Nehe areas. It is reported that several large detachments of Chinese troops are advancing towards the western section of the China Eastern Railway. Battles on the Songpu Front Lines Ongoing 27

(Harbin) The battles on the Songpu front lines are ongoing. Yesterday, it was reported that the anti-Manchukuo forces were gradually retreating. The sound of artillery fire could still be heard occasionally. Four bridges east of Hengdaohezi were destroyed yesterday. (Reuters dispatch, 19th)

Hengdaohezi Attacked by Bandits 28

(Harbin) According to reports from engineers on the Hengdaohezi-Suifenhe section, Hengdaohezi was attacked by bandits yesterday morning, and ten Russian and thirteen Chinese employees of the China Eastern Railway were abducted. The engineers requested that troops be dispatched immediately and that women and children in the nearby area be evacuated first. If troops arrive too late, other railway employees will either be abducted or killed. Yesterday, 600 bandits occupied Liudaohezi, eight miles east of Shitouhezi, and the wife of the deputy stationmaster was injured. (Reuters dispatch, 19th)

Kazantaiwo Stationmaster Escapes Danger 31

(Harbin) Mr. Ashenchik, the stationmaster of Kazantaiwo, who was abducted by bandits on April 20th, was released after his relatives and friends raised a ransom of 700 yuan. When Mr. Ashenchik was abducted as a stationmaster, his relatives and friends requested the Railway Bureau to prepare 1,000 yuan to redeem him, but the Railway Bureau refused. Most of the staff at the eastern section of the China Eastern Railway have lost everything due to repeated disturbances, and the Railway Bureau has not yet made any statement on compensating their losses. If disturbances occur in the western section in the future, railway staff will inevitably abandon their posts with all their belongings. (Reuters dispatch, 20th)

Zhou Zhenlin Invited to Visit Nanyue 41

Wang and Chen's Troops Jointly Suppress Peng's Bandits 42

Most of the Guangdong Army Advances Towards Yudu and Ruijin 43

(Nanchang) Most of the Guangdong army is advancing towards Yudu and Ruijin. Round Table Conference

The Time to Convene Has Not Yet Arrived 50

The Shanghai Incident and the Northeast Incident have a very strong connection and cannot be dealt with piecemeal. Therefore, the convening of this conference should wait until the Japanese troops have completely withdrawn from Chinese territory. (Special dispatch, 20th)

Niu Yongjian

Issues Important Statement 51

(Luoyang) Niu Yongjian, Vice President of the Examination Yuan, issued an important statement to our agency's reporter on the 19th regarding examination issues and Sino-Japanese issues, as follows:

Regarding Examination Issues 52

The Chinese nation is an excellent and intelligent nation in the world, with many talented people. It is a pity that the examination system has not yet been strictly implemented, resulting in the sigh of "lost treasures in the sea." The Examination Yuan should vigorously promote the examination system. Therefore, after the higher-level examinations last autumn, it was originally scheduled to hold general examinations this spring, but due to the need to deal with the national crisis, it was implicitly suspended. After the national crisis is resolved, the examination system should be strictly implemented to select true talents to create a new China based on the Three Principles of the People.

Regarding Sino-Japanese Issues 53

Currently, although Japan has withdrawn its troops from Shanghai, it is increasing its troops in the three northeastern provinces. Its conspiracy must be to take advantage of the League of Nations Investigation Team's presence in China to seize Pingjin in order to make demands as a fallback. Therefore, the situation in Yuguan is urgent, and there is a sense of imminent danger. This Sino-Japanese agreement in Shanghai certainly does not have any secret clauses that betray our country. Guangdong has fully understood this, and the situation in Guangdong has returned to normal. Our country must be fully prepared for a long-term resistance to deal with the violent Japanese. At the same time, we also hope that the League of Nations will provide just assistance to restrain Japan. However, the Japanese militarists insist on a hard-line stance and are secretly borrowing money from France. If successful, they will make a stubborn attack on us. A second world war is likely to break out in the Pacific, and our country cannot but engage in a final resistance. Winning the war can strengthen the country, and losing the war can also strengthen the country. If Japan loses the war, it will certainly perish, and even if it wins, it will also perish. Because China's war against Japan will surely unite the patriotic power of the entire 400 million people and fight to the death. However, the true Yamato race in Japan is only three or four million. There are differences in opinions among domestic parties, and we have the majority while they have the minority. We have spirit, while they have material. Who will win and who will lose? Moreover, various imperialists cannot sit idly by. It is a pity that the "wooden clog boy" cannot see through this simple logic and is willing to walk the path of destruction, which is very pitiful. We hope that at this critical moment of life and death, the entire country will be of one mind and unite sincerely, eliminate internal strife forever, and resist foreign aggression together. Only then can we save the country from danger. (Central News Agency dispatch, 20th)

Foreign News

Japanese Political Situation Remains Chaotic 97

Young Officers Strongly Oppose a Single-Party Cabinet

Seiyukai President Fails to Persuade Military

Saionji Tends to Favor the Military's Wishes

Hiranuma Cabinet Rumors Gain Traction

The Far East News Agency reported from Tokyo on the 20th that the political situation in Japan regarding the formation of a cabinet is deadlocked between the Seiyukai faction, led by the new president Suzuki, and the military, which advocates a national unity cabinet. Although the new Seiyukai president Suzuki dispatched Secretary-General Mori Kakuei to make great efforts to persuade Army Minister Araki and key figures in the military, the young officers in the military strongly opposed a single-party Seiyukai cabinet and had no effect. The military still insists that unless the ideal cabinet of the military is realized, no matter which faction rises to form a cabinet, there will be considerable methods to deal with it. Last night, Interior Minister Suzuki summoned Minister of Education Hatoyama and Secretary Mori to discuss the policy to cope with the situation. The result was still a decision to oppose a coalition or unified cabinet and to insist that a single-party Seiyukai cabinet was the only way forward. Therefore, the confrontation between the Seiyukai faction and the military has not only failed to ease slightly, but has worsened. As a result, the Genro Saionji, the protagonist in resolving the Japanese political situation, although he arrived in Tokyo at 5:00 PM yesterday, is unable to decide to enter the palace and make a request due to the extreme and uncompromising state of the two factions. Saionji is quite anxious about the deterioration of the situation. At 9:00 AM today, he summoned acting Prime Minister Takahashi, at 10:00 AM Privy Council President Kuratomi, and at 11:00 AM Army Minister Araki to his residence in Surugadai to listen to their opinions in an urgent attempt to find a way to enter the palace and request the Emperor to order the formation of a cabinet. However, according to the current situation, Saionji's entry into the palace to make a request may be difficult to achieve in the next day or two, and the trend of the Japanese political situation is not optimistic.

Domei News Agency reported from Tokyo on the 20th that Seiyukai President Suzuki invited Education Minister Hatoyama and Secretary-General Mori to the Interior Minister's official residence at 7:30 PM last night to discuss how to cope with the situation. At the meeting, it was believed that the military's demands on the successor cabinet could be divided into two factions. One faction argued that even a single-party cabinet was acceptable if it could implement the policies demanded by the military. The other faction absolutely opposed a single-party cabinet on principle. Since the military's own opinions were not consistent, it was decided to wait and see. This was the unanimous opinion. However, President Suzuki and Education Minister Hatoyama believed that organizing a single cabinet and implementing the military's demands was sufficient. Secretary Mori believed that it would be impossible to resolve the situation unless a national unity cabinet was organized, and it would be difficult to hope for the Emperor's command without the intention of organizing a national unity cabinet. Finally, President Suzuki stated that if Saionji requested him to form a cabinet on the condition of organizing a national unity cabinet or a cooperative cabinet, he would firmly decline.

Seiyukai Upholds Constitutionalism 98

Repudiates Pan-Nationalist Movement

Suzuki Formally Takes Office as President

Domei reported from Tokyo on the 20th that at today's temporary meeting of the Seiyukai, Secretary-General Yamaguchi strongly advocated that in order to establish constitutional politics, party politics must be upheld. Party elder Sugawara Den also strongly advocated, saying that President Inukai fought for constitutionalism until he was assassinated, and the will of the former president should be inherited to fight to the death against the fascist movement with an absolute majority of 300 members, and that the entire party should unite and strive for constitutional politics and uphold the new president.

Domei News Agency reported from Tokyo on the 20th that the Seiyukai held a party conference at its headquarters at 2:00 PM today and formally endorsed Interior Minister Suzuki as the next president. Next, the new President Suzuki gave a speech of thanks and took office, and the conference adjourned.

Reuters reported from Tokyo on the 20th that Suzuki's speech vigorously promoted the two major policies of consolidating national defense and improving existing diplomatic methods. Suzuki not only spoke of the need for national awareness, but also said that it was urgent to find ways to relieve the current economic distress, especially to focus on rural areas. Suzuki advocated clarifying politics and guiding the thoughts of the people.

Military's Attitude Hardens 99

Firmly Insists on Organizing a National Cabinet

Domei reported from Tokyo on the 20th that at this morning's meeting of the three chiefs of the Japanese Army, there was absolute opposition to a party cabinet, and all opinions were firmly excluded in order to realize a national unity cabinet. The military believes that after the completion of political purification by a national unity cabinet, the path of constitutionalism should be restored to normalcy. Therefore, at a time when the nation is facing survival, it does not care even if the world criticizes the military for interfering in politics.

Domei reported from Tokyo on the 20th that the opinion of the highest-ranking officers of the Army was originally to temporarily realize the Suzuki cabinet based on policy and then make further plans. As of last night, after the compromise theory between Suzuki and Araki was reported, the atmosphere in the department suddenly hardened, and it did not recognize the politics of political parties. Even with the prestige of Army Minister Araki and Vice Minister Masaki, if they were forcibly suppressed, there was a risk of an unforeseen incident. Therefore, the Army Minister and Vice Minister had no choice but to follow the general trend. Suzuki, Hatoyama, Mori, and others, seeing this situation, specially gathered last night to secretly discuss countermeasures and did not disperse until late at night. Judging from the current situation, unless Suzuki abandons his position as President of the Seiyukai and returns to the position of a patriot, he may not be able to wear the seal of the successor Prime Minister.

Reuters reported from Tokyo on the 20th that Army Training Inspector-General Takenouchi Nobuyoshi, accompanied by Deputy Chief of Staff Masaki, visited Army Minister Araki this morning and informed him of the Japanese Army's lack of preparation to support a purely party cabinet. Because the Army deeply believes that only a transcendental cabinet is sufficient to maintain the people's hearts, for the sake of supporting the country and safely navigating the current crisis, it is necessary to organize a non-partisan national government. Someone indicated that the Emperor may summon Hiranuma Shinsuke, the leader of the Kokuhonsha, tomorrow and order him to form a cabinet.

Domei reported from Tokyo on the 20th that junior officers of the Army and other like-minded people presented 13 articles of opinion to Army Minister Araki today, one of which stated, "A formed political party cannot be the basis for a new cabinet," which has already shown the attitude of the middle-ranking cadres of the Army towards the current situation.

Origin of Japan's Kokuhonsha 102

Organization Formed After Toranomon Incident

China United News Agency reported from Tokyo on the 20th that the Kokuhonsha was an organization created by Kōzō Ōta, a student at Tokyo Imperial University, at the end of 1919 to oppose the democracy movement of Dr. Yoshino. In 1924, when the Emperor was to pass through Toranomon by car for the opening ceremony of the Diet, he was assassinated. The Yamamoto Cabinet resigned because of this. After Justice Minister Hiranuma resigned from his position, he changed his policy and reorganized the Kokuhonsha into a thought group, starting a movement for national essence throughout the country, expanding its organization. Currently, Navy Minister Ōsumi and Army Minister Araki are its powerful leaders. Its power has infiltrated the military and the Ministry of Justice. Many other officials and financial leaders are maintainers of the association. Currently, the Kokuhonsha includes Sumitomo Bank General Manager Ikeda Seihin, former Justice Minister Hara Yoshimichi, former Ambassador Honda Kumataro, Upper House Member Viscount Ogasawara Nagasei, former Chief of Naval General Staff Katō Kanji, Vice Chief of Staff Masaki, Vice Minister of the Army Koiso, and Kantō Governor-General Yamaoka, among others. This shows its full composition. It utilizes the power of the Nichiren sect to promote feudal morality and is now the basic group of the Fascist Party in Japan's military and bureaucracy.

New Political Party Born 103

Domei reported from Tokyo on the 20th that the National Socialist Party held a general committee at this headquarters at 1:00 PM yesterday. Akamatsu Katsumaro, Hirano Rikizo, Koike Shiro and others attended, and as a result of discussing the establishment of a joint new party, it was decided to hold a party convention on the 29th and rename it the National Japan Party. Akamatsu et al. submitted a resolution to Lord Saionji at 6:00 PM in the afternoon, the gist of which was to hope to exclude the capitalist party and establish a cabinet that could represent the will of the people.

Soviet Official Denies

Military Demonstration Against Japan 104

TASS, Moscow, 20th - TASS has received an official announcement that firmly denies certain recent sensational reports from newspapers and news agencies, which mislead the public and diminish the value of the Soviet Union's commitment to a policy of peace. One report, disseminated by the German overseas news agency, concerned an address to the entire nation by the Red Army General Staff after the assassination of Japanese Prime Minister Inukai. According to the overseas news agency, this address was broadcast wirelessly throughout the Soviet Union. The Chief of the Red Army General Staff allegedly stated that in the coming weeks, it would be determined whether Japanese diplomats or Japanese military personnel would decide the policy towards Manchuria, and concluded by urging the Red Army to intensify preparations. The Soviet Union officially states that neither the Chief of the Red Army General Staff nor any other Soviet personnel made such an address. This report is clearly fabricated by the overseas agency and can only be viewed as an anti-Soviet fabrication. Another report, published yesterday in the New York Times and circulated by overseas news agencies, claimed that the Moscow Supreme Military Council had decided to call up reservists born in 1909, 1910, 1911, and 1912 for this year's grand maneuvers, to join the city security forces, or to join the Red Guards, with no exceptions allowed. The official statement indicates that the Supreme Military Council has made no such decision. The report from the overseas agency is groundless and can only be regarded as an anti-Soviet fabrication.

TASS, Moscow, 20th - Voskretsov, commander of the Far Eastern Red Army of the Soviet Union, who repeatedly defeated the White Russian forces during the civil war and foreign intervention, has passed away here. During the war, Voskretsov captured the city of Spassk, defeated the White Russian forces led by Dachlish, defeated the White Russian forces of Panbilev in Ogzhaksk, and captured Pan alive. For these achievements, Voskretsov received four Orders of the Red Banner.

Russian Representative

Proposes New Standards for Arms Reduction 109

National News Agency, Geneva, 19th - The Soviet Russian representative today proposed a new standard for arms reduction, requesting that each country's military strength be determined according to the following five points: (1) the length of coastline and land borders; (2) the size of the national territory and the density of the population; (3) the railway system; (4) military alliances and international political relations; (5) the degree of security enjoyed since the armistice of the European War. It strongly advocated that the fifth item should take into account whether the country has been subjected to foreign military invasion since the European War, or whether there have been other attempts to encroach upon its territory, before determining the extent of its military strength. In addition, the Russian representative also suggested strict restrictions on private capital invested in the manufacture of military equipment, and that the capital of all arsenals should be published on a regular basis.
