Important News

Japanese Deeply Fear 111

Sovietization of Japan

Fear of Taking the Opportunity to Disrupt the Pacific War with the United States

Transforming Yamato Japan into Soviet Japan

Therefore, They Want to Compromise with Soviet Russia Before the War

The Osaka Asahi Shimbun published an essay by Hirokichi Otake on the 13th, detailing the relationship between Soviet Russia and Japan, advocating for the easing of Soviet Russia's anti-Japanese sentiment, and discussing the attitude that Russia would take if war were to break out between Japan and the United States. This is extremely important, given the rapidly changing situation in the Far East. The attitudes of the United States and Russia toward Japan, and the strategies that Japan should adopt toward the United States and Russia, are matters of concern to those who are interested in the current situation. Therefore, we have translated it in order to prepare for future major changes. The full text is as follows:

The relationship between Japan and the Soviet Union is gradually shifting from tension to relaxation, judging from the recent atmosphere. The idea of a war between our Japan and the Soviet Union has not yet reached the stage of liquidation, so we should make every effort to avoid conflict between the two countries. Even if the Soviet Union challenges us, we are willing to retreat. Since Tanaka inspected Manchuria and returned home to express his views, the government has also tended to soften its stance toward Russia. Since the Manchurian Incident, although various difficulties have arisen in the future construction projects of Japan in Manchuria, the Soviet government, in the midst of the first five-year plan that has just been successfully completed, still has countless obstacles to domestic construction that have not yet been started to clear. Therefore, during this period, if a conflict occurs with Japan, its harmfulness and uselessness are also well known to the world. Moreover, after a conflict between Japan and Russia, it will inevitably involve the whole world and be involved in the vortex of war. The governments of the two countries, Japan and Russia, which bear such a major responsibility, dare not proceed rashly and take such a great risk. Since there is such a significant danger in fact, it can be clearly understood that conflicts will not occur from the current positions of the two countries.

However, where is the reason why the relations between the two countries cannot be stabilized today? The various problems that have arisen since the Manchurian Incident are often suspected by both sides. If we want to clear up this suspicion, there is no concrete or major strategy other than stabilizing the relations between Japan and Russia. The first way to stabilize Japan and Russia is to first establish coordination between Japan and Russia.

When the Manchurian Incident broke out last September, I happened to be traveling in the Soviet Union. The attitude of the government and the general society of that country towards the incident was speculated by foreigners residing in the Soviet Union at that time, and it was said that there was a secret agreement between Japan and Russia. However, the Japanese government and the public at that time thought that the obstruction to the actions in Manchuria was actually Soviet Russia. Afterwards, as the incident gradually shifted, the attitude of Soviet Russia became more cautious, and our people also did not examine the attitude of Soviet Russia, which led to the concentration of the Red Army on the Far Eastern border. At that time, the Japanese government and the public suddenly heard that the Red Army was moving east, which was almost like a bolt from the blue. Because in the era when the military preparations in the Far East were weak, the Soviet Russia, which outwardly pretended to be peaceful and strictly neutral, suddenly changed to a positive attitude today, which caused unrest among the people. This is the source of Japan's suspicion of Soviet Russia.

Although, it is not unreasonable for Soviet Russia to increase troops in the Far East. They believe that White Russian people are receiving open or secret assistance from Japan, attempting to disrupt the Far East. Therefore, Soviet Russia has to be prepared. Among them, Soviet Russia feels even more uneasy about Japan, that is, when Ambassador Aizawa was en route to Moscow in the past, the Russian government expressed the issue of a non-aggression treaty, and Ambassador Drolenov also proposed the intention of that issue. However, at that time, Japan thought that there was no need to conclude it. Therefore, Soviet Russia suspected that Japan had other ambitions. We believe that if there is no other intention in the Far East, we should urgently dispel Russia's misunderstanding. Secondly, Japan has declared its respect for the interests of Soviet Russia in the Middle East Railway. At present, White Russian people who are employed by Manchuria along the Middle East Railway, such as police officers and other positions, are quite active. Cases of intimidation of Soviet Russian people among railway employees are often heard. This time, the White Russian bombing of a military train suddenly deteriorated the relationship between Soviet Russia and Japan. This kind of instigation behavior of the White Russian people (the journalist notes that the Japanese side once pointed out that the explosion of the Middle East Railway military train was caused by Red Russia, but now suddenly says that it was instigated by White Russia, which is very strange) almost led to a conflict between Japan and Russia.

At that time, Soviet Russia prepared to negotiate with Japan on this issue and the general issue of the Middle East Railway, thinking that Japan's actions, which did not clearly indicate formal procedures, gained Russia's permission, and went its own way, which was difficult to tolerate. Therefore, Russia's suspicion of Japan is very strong. Fortunately, the people in charge of both countries recently worked hard to avoid conflict, and the situation has gradually eased. At this time, Japan and Soviet Russia should sincerely discuss the Manchuria issue to make Soviet Russia's doubts about Japan disappear.

However, when we silently observe the internal situation in Russia, there is indeed a very frightening point, that is, if Japan goes to war with the United States in the Pacific, Soviet Russia will definitely take advantage of the opportunity from behind to try to destroy Japan, plan to disrupt the domestic situation in Japan, and make the whole country fall into the red situation. Soviet Russia uses the good opportunity of the Japanese-American war, hoping that when Japan is defeated, it can take advantage of the confusion of the Japanese people's hearts to vigorously promote the redification of Japan in order to achieve the goal of world revolution. Therefore, some people advocate that before the Japanese-American war breaks out, we should first attack Soviet Russia to eliminate future troubles.

As for the Japanese-American war, from the observation of Russian politicians, it is a conflict between imperialism and imperialism. If Russia actively assists one side and makes another country win, it also violates the spirit of the founding of the Soviet Russia. However, Soviet Russia takes advantage of the opportunity of the Japanese-American war, rushes behind Japan, and transforms "Yamato Japan" into "Soviet Japan", which is difficult for us to guarantee that it will not do so. At that time, the situation in Japan, the enemy behind it, will increase the threat and hatred a hundredfold compared to the enemy in front. How will the national sentiment of the Japanese people be affected? It is also unknown. I am afraid that the Japanese government will have to negotiate peace with the enemy in front before a thorough defeat. At this time, the capitalist homeland of America, seeing that Japan has become Sovietized, will change its plan, unite with the anti-Soviet Western European countries, and stand on the same battle line to fight to the death with the Soviet Union. Therefore, this policy of Soviet Russia is also very risky.

Anhui Bandits Capture Huoqiu 112

Su Jiabu in Liu'an Also Falls

Huo and Shou Counties Request Troops to Suppress Bandits

Correspondent in Bengbu: Anhui bandits attacked and captured Zhengyang. Huoqiu was the first to receive a serious threat. After the bandits withdrew from Zhengyang, Huoqiu was reported to have fallen, indicating the rampant momentum of the bandits. Huoqiu is west of Zhengyang, south of Yingshang, bordering Liu'an to the south, and adjacent to Gushi on the Henan border to the west. The four southwestern townships have long been occupied by bandits. The 40th Brigade of Song Shike's division has been stationed in Huoqiu for more than a year. Due to effective maintenance in the past, there have been no accidents. When Zhengyang fell, the Cheng and Wang regiments of that brigade advanced from Huoqiu towards Zhengyang. Unexpectedly, the bandits took advantage of the emptiness in the city, gathered a large force to attack, and captured it on the 15th. Song's brigade immediately gathered around Yuezhangji to counterattack at the right time. After the fall of Huoqiu, the Huoqiu fellow villagers' association here received a telegram from Huoqiu local figures from Yingshang, pleading with the military authorities in Bengbu to request that a large army be dispatched quickly to suppress the bandits in order to save the survivors. After receiving the telegram, the association telegraphed the central government and Chen Tiaoyuan, requesting that troops be sent quickly to suppress the bandits. The area around Yingshang, Liu'an, Fengtai, and Shou County is now extremely tense. Su Jiabu in Liu'an, which had been besieged by bandits for many days, also fell due to lack of reinforcements a few days ago. Liu'an has been surrounded and is in urgent need of assistance. The 7th Aviation Squadron stationed in Bengbu has been dispatching aircraft to deliver supplies for days. Shou County, because no reinforcements have arrived for a long time, local militias and county police have jointly organized a city defense team. The people of Shou County in Bengbu have specially organized the Shou County Refugee Appeal Association. The association was informed that the Fourth Division had dispatched two brigades, but the division commander, Xu Tingyao, had not arrived, and the troops were unable to depart. Today (18th), representatives Yu Yumen, Lu Chewu, Sun Qiqian, etc., were specially dispatched to Beijing to appeal, urging Xu to come quickly and lead the troops to suppress the bandits, and appealed to the central government to send more troops to severely suppress the Red bandits in northern Anhui to save the people's lives and secure the locality. (18th)

Hunan, Guangdong, and Jiangxi Armies 113

Encircle and Suppress Peng Dehuai

Recapture of Rucheng, Still Deadlocked in Guidong

Guangdong and Jiangxi Armies Arrive for Another Joint Encirclement and Suppression

Correspondent in Changsha: After the failure of the 5th Army of the 3rd Army Corps of the Red bandits, Peng Dehuai, and the 7th Army of Li Mingrui (after Li's death, the troops were commanded by Peng concurrently), they fled to the Shangyou and Chongyi areas. In late April, because He Jian sent Hou Pengfei's brigade stationed in Chenzhou to resolve the old troops of Gong Hao stationed in Yizhang, Hunan, and chased into Guiyang and Jiahe in Hunan, the defense of Chenzhou was empty. Peng Dehuai took the opportunity to enter Hunan and occupied Rucheng on May 2nd, and occupied Guidong on the 8th, with a great intention to invade southern Hunan. He Jian immediately telegraphed Wang Dongyuan, commander of the 15th Division, to reorganize the old troops of Gong Hao into the training regiment of the 15th Division to resolve the issue. He immediately transferred Hou Pengfei's brigade back to Chenzhou to block Peng's bandits, and convened a military conference in Changsha on the 11th to discuss the suppression plan. He Jian, Liu Jianxu, Li Jue, Peng Weiren, etc. were all present and agreed on the following matters: (1) Wang Dongyuan's division, Hou Pengfei and Zhang Guzhong's two brigades, and the local defense forces of Chenzhou, Rucheng, and Guiyang will advance from Chenzhou to suppress Rucheng, with Wang Dongyuan as the commander of the front line; (2) Chen Guangzhong's division, Zhao Mengyan's brigade, and the teams of Anling and other counties will advance from Ling County towards Guidong, with Chen Guangzhong as the commander of the front line; (3) The aviation department was ordered to send Yan Yaopu of the First Aviation Squadron to lead three aircraft to Hengzhou, and to fly to Rucheng and Guiyang every day for reconnaissance and bombing; (4) Wang Dongyuan's division, Wang Zhibin's brigade, and the teams of the four counties of Hengyang, Hengshan, Changning, and Leiyang will be the general reserve team, concentrated in Leiyang and Yongxing, and will reinforce Rucheng and Guiyang at any time; (5) All the above-mentioned troops are limited to completing the concentration by the evening of the 12th, and a general offensive will be launched towards Rucheng and Guiyang at dawn on the 13th; (6) He Jian and Liu Jianxu will depart from the province to Heng and Chen on the 13th to supervise the suppression; (7) The above-mentioned suppression plan will be telegraphed to Jiangxi He (Yingqin) and Guangdong Chen (Jitang) to request their dispatch of troops to encircle and suppress the bandits in order to achieve encirclement. After the above mobilization order was issued, Wang Dongyuan took a car from Hengzhou to Chenzhou on the 12th. On the 13th, he supervised Hou and Zhang's two brigades to attack Rucheng. The Peng bandits in Rucheng, known as the Second and Third Divisions, with about 3,000 people, only made contact for about two hours in Maqiao, 30 miles away from Rucheng, and then abandoned Rucheng and fled to the Reshuiwei and Wenying areas. Hou's brigade recovered Rucheng at 1 p.m. on the 13th. Because the Reshuiwei and Wenying areas are adjacent to Jiangxi, it is necessary to wait for the arrival of the Guangdong and Jiangxi armies before they can be jointly suppressed. Therefore, Hou and Zhang's two brigades are temporarily stationed in Rucheng awaiting orders. As for Zhao Mengyan's brigade, which attacked Guidong, because the journey from Ling County to Guidong is full of high mountains and inconvenient transportation, it did not arrive near Guidong until the 15th. The Red bandits in Guidong had one division of Peng Dehuai and two regiments of Li Mingrui. They came into contact on the 16th, and because of their strong resistance, the two sides were still deadlocked until the 18th. He Jian took a car from the province to Hengzhou on the morning of the 13th, and then went to Leiyang on the morning of the 14th. He arrived at 11 a.m., convened the general reserve team for training, and then went to Chenzhou from Leiyang at 12 o'clock to inspect. On the 15th, he returned to Leiyang from Chenzhou to arrange everything. On the 16th, he returned to Hengzhou from Leiyang and negotiated with the army commander Liu Jianxu: (1) All matters concerning the suppression of bandits in southern Hunan in the future will be handed over to Liu Jianxu. All the troops, teams, and aircraft currently in southern Hunan will be under Liu's command and dispatch. He Jian returned to the province that day; (2) Order the general reserve team in Leiyang and Yongxing to rush to Guidong to assist in the attack, and strive to recover Guidong County within three days; (3) After the recovery of Guidong, the various army groups will stop in Rucheng and Guidong to await orders, and will wait for the Guangdong and Jiangxi armies to establish contact with the Hunan army before carrying out a joint encirclement and suppression.

As for the troops sent by Guangdong and Jiangxi to join the suppression, the provincial government received telegrams from He Yingqin and Chen Jitang yesterday, stating that Jiangxi Province sent two divisions of Chen Cheng's department, Li Ming and Liu Shaoxian, and Guangdong Province sent three brigades of Chen Zhang, Chen Hanguang, and Fan Dexing, all advancing towards Rucheng and Guiyang on the Hunan border to suppress the bandits. The three provinces of Hunan, Guangdong, and Jiangxi now have five divisions with five military forces, which will launch a large-scale encirclement of the bandits. (May 18th)

Songjiang

Request to Survey and Repair Seawall Again 114

The seawall along the county's coast is in a precarious state and urgently needs repair. The county chamber of commerce has telegraphed the seawall committee to appeal. Now, it continues to telegraph its petition, saying: "Jiangnan Seawall Committee of the Jiangsu Provincial Construction Department, greetings. The resolution of the seawall conference to convene this session to determine the order of projects will be truly beneficial to the coastal people. However, the Songjiang seawall is divided into first, second, third, and fourth sections, and must be repaired as a whole to achieve solidity. The first and second sections were originally earthen seawalls, and danger occurred here last year, with a breach of a hundred feet, shocking far and wide. If there is a storm this autumn, the earthen seawall will be washed away first, and the third and fourth sections, no matter how strong, will have no guarantee. We sincerely request that the four sections of the Songjiang seawall be surveyed and repaired together at the same time. In addition to the lack of funds, there are very large old straight stones that should be moved to the most important places to defend. The association has more immediate knowledge and is deeply fearful. We respectfully plead for the lives of hundreds of thousands of compatriots along the coast. We look forward to the implementation with the utmost anticipation."

Jiangyin 118

Suicide by Poisoning Due to Economic Pressure On the evening of the 16th, at about 9 p.m., a traveler, Wang Baoshan, who was staying at the Zhaoshang Hotel on Dongda Street, room 32, was asleep. He did not get up until 11 a.m. on the 17th. Zhou Baoyuan, the tea house attendant, knocked on the door but received no response. Then he heard a groan from the next room and quickly knocked on the door. Only then did he know that he had taken poison. A suicide note was left on the table, stating that he had committed suicide because he was under economic pressure and his aunt and uncle Zhou Zixiang in Zhoujiawan suspected him of stealing gold jewelry in order to clear his name. Afterwards, he was sent to the Red Cross Hospital for gastric lavage by the hotel, but it was ineffective and he died soon after. In the afternoon, the Public Security Bureau reported to the county for examination and summoned Zhou Zixiang for questioning before ordering him to collect the body.

Playing with Bombs Leads to Instant Death in Wenlin Township, Hexiang 119

A villager named Shen Ada from the iron alley of Hexiang Bridge in Wenlin Township found a bomb in the field and took it home. Later, a fellow villager named Qian Erbao saw it and began playing with it. Unexpectedly, it exploded with a loud bang, killing Erbao instantly. The district chief, Huang Baoquan, reported the incident to the county government, which dispatched officials to investigate.

Qingjiang 120

Bandits Set Fire to Kill Five in Huaiyin Yugou Dongwei. The home of Gao Yundou, outside the eastern embankment of Yugou in Huaiyin, was attacked by dozens of bandits in the first half of the night on the 12th. Failing to break in, the bandits became enraged and set fire to Gao's house in four places. As a result, five members of Gao's family of ten were burned to death, Yundou himself suffered severe injuries and his life is in danger, and the remaining four members also suffered burns to their heads and feet. The news is truly tragic.

Gaoyou 121

The Commissioner Orders a Thorough Investigation of Embankment Construction Case.颜作宾 (Yan Zuobin) from Baoying, previously changed the route when constructing the southern embankment of Baoying, forcibly digging up farmland in Gaoyou and arbitrarily arresting farmers' representatives Shen Furong and others. They have not yet been released. Previously, more than fifty farmers from the tenth district, including Liu Tianguan, sent a telegram to the provincial government's Construction Department, accusing Yan of various illegal acts. It is now reported that the department yesterday ordered the county government to thoroughly investigate and report.

Pinghu 122

The Reason for Xu Difan's Suicide. Xu Difan, a female doctor at the Deji Hospital, was originally from Wuxi. Her parents and two younger sisters lived at home. Five years ago, she was introduced to work at the Deji Hospital. Because of her plain appearance, Xu had told people that she intended to remain single. Although she was thirty years old, she was not yet married. She was quite dedicated to her work, and her obstetrical surgeries were considered the best in Pingyi. Over the years, she had gained the praise of local people, and her business flourished as a result. The hospital owner, Wang Yu Jiu, was delighted to have her as an assistant and treated her generously. Xu, feeling adrift in the world, was usually pessimistic. Since meeting Wang and spending time together, an unspoken relationship developed between them. Recently, Wang's wife found out about it and, consumed by jealousy, took the opportunity to humiliate and scold her. Xu couldn't help but feel sorry for herself and cried loudly in her room all night. Although Wang's wife apologized and Wang comforted her, she was already determined to die and could not be dissuaded. That night, she ran out the window, intending to take a boat to Shanghai. Wang noticed and quickly chased her to the pier and persuaded her to return. The next day, Xu, taking advantage of people's inattention, secretly went to Shanghai. She sent two registered letters from the Lao Huizhong Hotel on Lishan East Road, one to Wang Yu Jiu and one to a colleague named Xu. Wang, upon reading the letter, knew that he had caused a disaster. He hastily sent his wife to Jiaxing to take a car to Shanghai, while he himself took a boat from Pinghu to Shanghai, hoping to prevent any mishaps. However, it was too late, and news of her death arrived. The people of Pingyi are all lamenting her death.

The Provisional Capital's Telephone Officially Opens. The Preparatory Office for the Provisional Capital's Telephone of the Ministry of Communications has been working hard to install telephone lines and machines, sparing no effort. As of yesterday morning, it was reported that they had installed telephone machines for fifty or sixty households. The chief engineer of the office, Du Chengjian, and engineer Zhu Yong, tested the phones by dialing numbers, and the results were extremely satisfactory. Therefore, at six o'clock yesterday morning, in the midst of heavy rain, they announced the official opening of the telephone service. The sound was very clear and distinct. In recent days, many users have been going to register and have machines installed.

Postal Workers' Union Telegrams the Ministry of Communications 125

Demanding Thorough Investigation of Bribery and Strike

Yesterday, the fundraising columns of various newspapers published news that the Ministry of Communications had received a secret report that someone had offered 30,000 yuan to instigate a strike by Shanghai postal workers. The content was quite bizarre. Yesterday, reporters from various newspapers visited Zhao, a committee member of the Shanghai Postal Workers' Union, to ask for his opinion on the matter and to inquire about the union's plan to strengthen the postal service and the recent progress. Zhao gave a comprehensive response. Reporter (Q): The Ministry of Communications telegraphed back to the General Post Office that the proposed merger of the Savings and Remittance Bureau should not be allowed after being decided by the Central Political Council. However, there were some substantial responses regarding other issues. How will your members respond to this? (A): The proposals submitted by our two unions and postal workers' unions across the country are divided into three main categories: maintaining the principle of self-sufficiency of the postal service, merging the Savings and Remittance Bureau, and stopping subsidies for airline expenses. Among them, the merger of the Savings and Remittance Bureau is the most important issue that employees across the country have been fighting for a long time and is the main purpose of this movement. However, the Ministry of Communications has determined that the merger of the Savings and Remittance Bureau should not be allowed, and there is no indication of agreement regarding the other two categories. What they have agreed to is only the restoration of the existing compensation system for our postal workers. In short, the Ministry of Communications' telegram shows no sincerity in accepting our union's plan to strengthen the postal service. Our two unions will continue to work hard and persevere. (Q): It is reported that Mayor Wu of Shanghai invited eight members of your union, including Shi Yitang and Zhao Shusheng, to a meeting at 3:00 PM the day before yesterday and expressed enthusiastic support for your plan, promising to pass it on to the central government for implementation. I wonder if this will achieve its purpose? (A): Our union has received reports from members Zhao Shusheng and Shi Yitang about this matter. We are very grateful for Mayor Wu's sympathy and kindness. With Mayor Wu's sympathy and leadership, we will surely benefit even more in practice. However, our union's approach is to respect the will of all employees, and we will not delay our efforts because of this. (Q): Regarding the news report that the Ministry of Communications received a secret report that someone offered 30,000 yuan to instigate a strike by Shanghai postal workers and has ordered the strike to be stopped and the ringleaders to be arrested, this news is quite bizarre. How will your union respond to this? (A): According to the news report, our union has telegraphed the Ministry of Communications to investigate the source of the secret report. As those responsible for the postal workers' union, our determination is very firm. We cannot be subdued by force or moved by self-interest. The so-called "movement of tens of thousands of yuan" may be a fabrication of charges by a group of political rascals attempting to undermine the postal service. However, our union firmly believes that the Ministry of Communications' decision must have a source. We hope that the truth will be clarified as soon as possible. If the Ministry of Communications confirms that this is indeed the case, then any member of our union is willing to go to Beijing and surrender themselves without waiting for the Ministry of Communications to arrest them. Otherwise, the person who made the secret report should be prosecuted to clarify their legal responsibility, etc. The committee member then showed the reporter the telegram sent to the Ministry of Communications, which is recorded below. To the Ministry of Communications in Nanjing: We have read today's Shanghai newspaper report that the Ministry of Communications received a secret report that someone offered 30,000 yuan to instigate a strike by Shanghai postal workers and that the Executive Yuan was requested to immediately telegraph the Shanghai Party, government, and military authorities to strictly stop it and arrest the ringleaders. We are extremely indignant. Our two unions have proposed a plan to strengthen the postal service as a long-term solution to protect the postal service. Our intentions are pure and can be testified to by Heaven and Earth. We urge you to investigate the source of the secret report. If it is indeed the case, our two unions are willing to lead more than 30,000 employees across the country to the capital to accept the most severe punishment. If it is false, please investigate and prosecute the person who made the secret report to clarify their legal responsibility and to dispel public doubts. Sincerely, Shanghai Postal Workers' Union and Postal Employees' Union.

The New Articles of Association of the Water Company 126

Provoke Widespread Opposition

The Real Estate Association Issues an Urgent Notice

The Shanghai British Waterworks Company of the Public Concession has implemented a new contract signed with the Municipal Council in 1931, adopting a water meter system. This has provoked widespread opposition, and the situation is quite serious. However, the water company has notified users in Zone 2 to sign the new contract by the end of May or face suspension of water supply. The Real Estate Association issued an urgent notice yesterday. The details are as follows:

Original Text of the Contract 127

The Public Concession Municipal Council and the Shanghai British Waterworks Company entered into a new contract on December 24, 1931, as follows: (1) The Company may, in all bills issued in January 1932 and subsequent months, charge for water supplied for municipal purposes and to users referred to in the contract at the rates specified in the attached table, in place of the current rates. The various prices listed in Article 2 of the contract dated February 18, 1930, are equal to the price of water supplied by standby pipes as stipulated in Clause 4 of Schedule C attached hereto. This water price also includes the aforementioned increased water price. (2) All price schedules include all incidental matters and may be amended at any time if both parties agree that there is a legitimate reason for amendment. Whenever the silver exchange rate rises to two shillings, the Municipal Council may reassess the aforementioned increased water price. (3) The Company shall immediately proceed to adopt a common water meter system throughout the entire area of water supply and shall therefore divide the supply area into appropriate sub-areas. These sub-areas should, as far as is conveniently possible, be paired, one being a sub-area with generally high rental values and one being a sub-area with generally low rental values. Each such pair of sub-areas, upon the completion of the common water meter system therein, shall be referred to as a "metered area" as referred to in the attached schedules. (4) Article 2 of the aforementioned contract dated February 28, 1930, shall not apply to users who use water solely for manufacturing purposes, that is, any user with a private well who can prove to the satisfaction of the Company that his business must use both well water and Company water and who, in addition to paying the meter rates specified in Clause 2 of Schedule C attached hereto, pays a monthly fee equal to the price of water supplied by standby water as specified in Clause 4 of Schedule C attached hereto, according to the size of the water pipe, may be supplied with water by the Company for manufacturing purposes. However, the application of this clause shall be limited to those who have already built water wells on the date of signing the main contract, and the Company may refuse to enter into a new contract to supply such water at any time if the Company deems that the supply of such water is not appropriate due to loss of revenue or any other reason, but shall notify the Municipal Council of its intention to refuse to supply such water within a reasonable period of time. (5) Schedule C attached to the aforementioned contract dated June 19, 1929, and Articles 3 and 4 of the contract dated February 28, 1930, are hereby repealed. [Signed] Li Lubokeer, Director, Shanghai Waterworks Company; Walker, Secretary; MacKean, Acting General Manager, Public Concession in the Foreign Settlement area north of the Shanghai Yangjingbang. (Note: Water Price Schedule C omitted.)

Opposition from All Sectors 128

The Citizens' Federation has decided to firmly oppose the implementation of the new water meter system by the British Waterworks Company, which increases the burden on citizens during a period of economic downturn after the war. It has decided to negotiate with the Municipal Council as soon as possible to oppose the new articles of association of the Waterworks Company and restore the original method, in order to reduce the burden on citizens. It has also requested the assistance of the Chinese Ratepayers' Association. The Chinese Ratepayers' Association has also sent a letter to the General Manager of the Municipal Council to correct the new articles of association of the Waterworks Company. The entire Chinese board of directors is studying and considering the case.

Urgent Notice 129

The Real Estate Association yesterday issued an urgent notice to its members, which reads as follows: "Dear Sirs, With reference to the waterworks issue discussed at the Association's general meeting on May 14, the following resolutions were passed: (1) All landlords are hereby notified to immediately dig their own wells for use, in order to avoid being arbitrarily exploited by monopolistic businesses. (2) All landlords are hereby notified to refuse to sign the new waterworks contract with unilateral demands and unilateral benefits, in order to avoid future troubles. Even if the water supply is cut off, the water cutoff will be held responsible for obstructing people's livelihood and peace. (3) A letter will be sent to the British Shanghai Waterworks Company to maintain the Association's original resolutions: (A) Water meters will not be collected on behalf of the company, in order to avoid losses from compensating or advancing water bills. (B) One water meter per household will ensure fairness and avoid situations where those who use less water pay more and those who use more water pay less. (C) Users shall not be responsible for the installation or deposit of water meters. (D) The water price is too high and does not meet the economic capacity of Shanghai users, nor does it comply with the good practices of a monopolistic business. The Association's original resolutions will be supplemented as follows: 'Before water meters are installed throughout the entire supply area, a flat rate system may be temporarily used, but when the water company voluntarily collects water bills directly from users, the water bill included in the flat rate rent should be deducted in accordance with the facts, and the users should pay it directly to the water company.' (4) A letter will be sent to the Municipal Council to inquire why the draft of the new contract with the water company was not published in advance to solicit users' opinions before it was signed and came into effect, and to state that the water company is attempting to force the signing of the new contract by cutting off the water supply, which is a sign of contempt for the status of our industry and a deliberate obstruction of people's livelihood and peace. The relevant information is hereby transmitted, and it is hoped that you will investigate and handle the matter accordingly, as it concerns the survival of our industry." (New Voice News Agency)

Countess Glanston 130

Talks About Impressions of Visiting China

The Terror of the Japanese Invasion of Shanghai

The Good Custom of the Chinese Respecting the Elderly

Reuters reported from London on the 19th that Countess Glanston gave a speech at the Overseas Companions Association today, detailing the impact of the Japanese bombing of Shanghai. She said that when she first arrived in Shanghai, she did not see the commercial recession that she had seen elsewhere. She was deeply surprised, as Shanghai was a prosperous area where everyone seemed happy. However, when she returned to Shanghai after touring the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, she saw that Shanghai's business and commerce were simply lifeless, and the streets were full of pitiful refugees fleeing from the war zone. The Countess remarked that she initially enjoyed her tour of China, but after the invasion, she was left with this terrible impression. When she was in China, her white hair was her most valuable treasure, because due to her age, the Chinese respected the elderly and treated her with courtesy. This is truly a rare and precious custom, she said.

The Newly Appointed General Manager of China National Aviation Corporation 133

Liu Peiquan Assumed Office Yesterday Morning

Liu Peiquan, the newly appointed General Manager of China National Aviation Corporation, assumed office at the company at 9:00 AM yesterday morning. The details are as follows:

Assumption of Office 134

At 9:00 AM yesterday morning, Liu, along with Nie Kaiyi, Deputy Director of the Aeronautical Engineering Group, and Wu Zhaoxuan, Chief Secretary, went to the company from their residence in Yian Lane on Albert Road by car to assume office. After arriving at the bureau, the British Deputy Chairman, Bender, introduced him to the former General Manager, He Jiwu. Liu then convened a meeting of all the company's staff for instructions, and the former General Manager He left first.

Changes in Staff 135

After Liu assumed office, some important staff members resigned one after another and could not be retained. Therefore, Wu Zhaoxuan, the former secretary of the Ministry of Communications, was appointed as the director of the Secretariat. He Zhiying, the former director, was transferred to serve as the deputy director of the Business Group. Guo Bairang was appointed as the director of the Finance Group. Nie Kaiyi, the former deputy director of the Aeronautical Engineering Group, has been transferred to the Ministry of Communications as a technician, but General Manager Liu has transferred him back to his original position in the company. There are no significant changes to other staff members.

Reporting the Assumption of Office 136

After assuming office, Liu immediately telegraphed the Ministry of Communications, the original telegram said: "To Minister Chen and Vice Minister Chen Yujun of the Ministry of Communications, The shareholders' meeting of China National Aviation Corporation was held the day before yesterday. All directors were elected in accordance with the personnel proposed by your ministry. At the same time, all resolutions of the second board of directors have been approved. Peiquan arrived at the bureau to take over the day before yesterday. In addition to reporting, I would like to telegraph you first. Liu Peiquan, General Manager of China National Aviation Corporation."

Dispatching Telegrams to Subordinates 137

Liu sent telegrams to all the company's offices and branches yesterday, which read: "To all offices and branches, This company's board of directors has been reorganized, and Peiquan has been appointed as the chairman and general manager. Peiquan officially assumed the position of general manager at the company at 9:00 AM today. In addition to reporting to the Ministry of Communications, this is to inform you that all service personnel in the branch should continue to work as usual, in order to jointly strive for the prosperity of the company. We sincerely hope for this. [Signed] Liu Peiquan, General Manager."

Liu's Instructions 138

Liu's instructions to the staff yesterday were roughly as follows: "China National Aviation Corporation has been established for many years. Thanks to the efforts of the former General Manager He, the achievements are very good. In the future, I will continue to follow the rules and regulations and continue the ambitions of the former General Manager He to continue to work hard. China's aviation industry has always been controlled by foreigners. After I take office, I plan to first organize an aviation school to train aviation talents. Secondly, I must establish a large-scale aircraft manufacturing plant to engage in manufacturing, so that we can recover the money spent on purchasing aircraft from overseas every year."

Inspecting the Airport 139

At about 2:00 PM, Liu, accompanied by Nie Kaiyi, Deputy Director of the Aeronautical Engineering Group, went to the company's seaplane base in Longhua by car to inspect it. He returned at 4:00 PM. The four directors elected by the company's shareholders are Chen Mingshu, Chairman of the Board; Liu Peiquan, Director and Deputy Chairman; Nie Kaiyi and Yang Jianping.

April 141

Japan's Foreign Trade Again Shows a Trade Deficit

The Japanese Commercial Counselor's Office in Shanghai received a telegram from Tokyo on the 19th stating that Japan's foreign trade in April showed a trade deficit of 49 million yen. The total value of exports for the month was 92 million yen, an increase of 12-13% compared to the same period last year. Exports of raw silk, cotton textiles, cotton yarn, and rayon cloth all saw significant increases. Imports of cotton, iron, kerosene, wool, wheat, and soybeans also saw significant increases. The total trade deficit for the first four months of this year has reached 20.8 million yen, an increase of 12.6 million yen compared to the same period last year. Trade with China in March of this year showed a trade surplus of 3 million yen, with a total export value of 23 million yen. The trade surplus in April was 6 million yen, with a total export value of 24 million yen. The total trade deficit for the first four months was 6 million yen, an increase of 4 million yen compared to the same period last year. The situation between China and Japan is gradually stabilizing, and exports are also gradually increasing. For example, comparing April with March, imports have decreased by 29%, while exports have increased by 2%. Exports to Central China decreased by 31%, to South China by 87%. Imports from Central China also decreased by 76%, from South China by 47%. Exports to North China increased by 51%, to Manchuria decreased by 36%. Imports from North China decreased by 48%, while imports from Manchuria increased by 5%.

The Citizens' Federation 142

Sends Letters to the Telephone and Waterworks Companies

Demanding at Least One Quarter of Free Service in the Hongkou Area

The Citizens' Federation sent letters to the Waterworks Company and the Telephone Company yesterday, which read: "According to a letter from the temporary office of the Hongkou District branch of our association, since the January 28th Incident, businesses throughout the city have been suspended and the financial system has stagnated. Residents in the war zone have been buried in the ravages of fire and the desolate fields. Those who were lucky enough to escape death could only flee and wander, enduring unspeakable misery. Even residents of the concession, who enjoy the security of the Municipal Council's police force, such as those in our Hongkou District, were occupied by the Japanese army as soon as the Shanghai Incident began, and the entire district was plunged into chaos. It suffered the scourge of war just like the war zone, and suffered even more from the massacre and torture of the Japanese army. Therefore, during the war, the footprints of the Chinese in areas such as our Hongkou were cut off, and the streets were like ghost towns. These facts are well known to both Chinese and foreigners. Now that the ceasefire agreement has been initially reached and residents are gradually gathering, it is expected that recovery will be difficult in the future. Therefore, our association proposes that the fees for telephone and water services, which were mostly unused during the war, should be waived for one quarter. This is the minimum requirement and is not an unreasonable request. We have informed all branches to notify all members to stop paying the fees until the negotiations are concluded, in order to alleviate the difficulties of businesses and help the market."

Two Trade Associations 145

Appeal to the Ratepayers' Meeting

Requesting Exemption from Donations

The North Zhejiang Road and Boundary Road trade associations yesterday sent a letter via a representative from the Anle Daqi Society to the Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the Concession, requesting them to negotiate with the Concession authorities for exemption from the spring general donation and the summer certificate donation. The original letter is as follows: "To the esteemed Shanghai Ratepayers' Association, we write to inform you that our districts, adjacent to the North Station and particularly at the intersection of the Chinese and Concession territories, have been under immense strain since the outbreak of the January 28th Shanghai Incident. Gates were firmly closed, guards were heavily enforced, and transportation was severed, leading to a complete standstill in commerce. The people here were in a state of utter isolation, surrounded by desolation, almost like an uninhabited area. Residents who could not escape had no way to survive. Even those who were fortunate enough to flee had no homes to return to. The extent of the losses suffered in these two to three months is immeasurable. Many were bankrupted by the war, and others have yet to reopen their businesses, accounting for more than half of the total. This is a testament to the terrifying state and severe hardship of those days, which is painful to even speak of. Recently, the municipal general donation and certificate donation have been collected with great urgency. Merchants and residents have suffered losses due to the war and their assets are completely depleted. With no avenue for appeal, they can only endure everything from the donation collectors without daring to resist. It is deeply regrettable that while merchants and residents have always fulfilled their tax obligations in the past, they are now losing their rights. We believe that exempting the spring general donation and the summer certificate donation for the period of the war is a proper relief measure. Therefore, we dare to present the details and request your association's Chinese directors to fight for our cause based on reason. We would be deeply grateful. Respectfully submitted to the Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers' Association."

England 146

Famous Female Explorer Arrives in Shanghai

Miss Clairesse Marks

The *North-China Daily News* reports that the famous British female explorer, Miss Clairesse Marks, arrived in Shanghai during her honeymoon trip around the world after marrying an Englishman, Mr. Fesyu, in California, USA, on March 13th of this year. Miss Marks is one of the world's most renowned female explorers. In the past nine years, she has often funded her own expeditions to rarely visited places. She once traveled within the Arctic Circle, from Lapland to Russia, accompanied only by four Lapland guides, traversing icy and snowy terrain for sixty-seven days. She has also explored the wilderness of Mexico and hunted wild beasts in the Rocky Mountains of America, the Himalayas of Asia, and the Congo of Africa. This year, she originally planned a second expedition to Tibet, but it was cancelled due to a tropical disease contracted last year on the banks of the Amazon River in South America, which required a long period of convalescence as advised by her doctor. Miss Marks is proficient in astronomy and drawing. Wherever she explores, she relies on astronomical observations to identify directions, draw maps, and collect scientific specimens. Many of her works are now housed in the British Museum and other institutions.

Mongolian Road Gate Opens Yesterday 147

After negotiations between Huang Ming, the Police Corps Commander of our city's Public Security Bureau and concurrently the Director of the Public Security Bureau's Shanghai North Office, and the工部局 (gōng bù jú, an administration board of the International Settlement), the gates at various locations on the border between the Zhabei Chinese area and the Concession, apart from the Wuzhen Road Bridge which was opened on the morning of the day before yesterday, the gate at the Mongolian Road entrance (next to the Xinsheng Theater) was also opened yesterday. It is also heard that the obstacles at the southern end of the Xinzhazha Bridge gate have also been completely removed yesterday in preparation for opening. However, the Concession authorities seem to require a slight delay as there are still Japanese soldiers north of the Zhabei Railway. It will be opened as soon as the Japanese Marine Corps in Zhabei completely withdraws.

Japanese Military Searching for Missing Japanese Soldiers 148

Fearing Drowning, Blocking Rivers to Search

The Japanese Marine Corps north of the Zhabei Railway, when on patrol near Zhonghua Xin Road and Pengpu Xin Bridge, had several Japanese soldiers suddenly disappear at night, along with several firearms. The Japanese Command suspected they had been hidden or harmed by local thugs, so the next morning, they imposed a special curfew, closing the railway gates at both Gonghe Xin Road and Taiyang Temple, prohibiting pedestrian traffic for two days. They also dispatched a large Marine Corps force of about three to four hundred men to search house to house north of the railway, without success. Afterwards, they sent soldiers with bamboo poles, iron hooks, and fishing nets to dredge various rivers, such as Zhangjia Bang, Tan Jia Wan, Su Huai, Yu Gang, and Tanzi Guan, but found no trace. Yesterday, it was heard that the Japanese military authorities, with the withdrawal from north of the railway imminent, needed to quickly investigate the missing Japanese soldiers and firearms. Therefore, yesterday they again dispatched a large Marine Corps force, carrying a large number of hemp bags and bamboo poles, and conscripted many laborers to fill hemp bags with mud, blocking the rivers, and draining the accumulated water to facilitate the search for the missing Japanese soldiers and firearms. However, from morning to dusk, they found nothing.

Enamel Industry Regulations Approved 152

The enamel industry is closely related to practical applications in the country's industries. There are more than ten factories in the Jin market. The annual output is tens of millions. It is an important industry that replaces imported goods. The industry established a trade association in 1925. They have been working hard to improve various aspects of the industry. Recently, they have been paying attention to the industry regulations of the same industry. Therefore, drafting industry regulations is their top priority. They drafted 22 articles of industry regulations and submitted them to the Social Affairs Bureau for record. After review by the Social Affairs Bureau, the regulations were deemed appropriate and approved for record. The Social Affairs Bureau issued instruction number 2041: "For the record, it has been found that the association submitted a case for industry regulations for approval. This Bureau has already given instructions to submit it to the Industry Regulations Review Committee for review. Now that the review is complete, the association’s regulations are deemed appropriate and should be approved. In addition to submitting a copy to the Municipal Government and sending separate letters to the Municipal Department of Public Security and other relevant departments, and publishing it in the Municipal Government Gazette, the industry regulations should be followed. The association should publish the regulations in the Shen Bao, Xinwen Bao, and cover advertisements for three days, and distribute them to all industry members for compliance. This order is issued. After receiving the order, the association should publish the announcement in the newspaper and distribute it to all industry members for implementation."

Results of a Meeting of Representatives from Five National Goods Groups

Another Philanthropist Dies Prematurely 154

Zhang Gongheng's Funeral Held Yesterday

Mr. Zhang Gongheng, Anhui Commissioner of the National Government's Flood Relief Committee, has been personally handling relief affairs for a year, without taking time to rest. This time, he came to Shanghai to discuss spring relief affairs in his province with the committee. Unfortunately, he contracted an epidemic and died in Shanghai despite medical treatment. Everyone who heard of Mr. Zhang's dedication to relief work and his sudden death could not help but sigh, and another person dedicated to philanthropy has passed away.

A Gruesomely Murdered Male Corpse Discovered Near Yu Family Cemetery 155

Some Say it Was Caused by an Affair with a Young Girl

A male corpse was recently discovered near the Yu family cemetery on Xietu Road in western Shanghai. After the local security officer reported it to the local court, the body was examined by Prosecutor Yang and others yesterday. The corpse was about thirty years old, the face was already decayed, and it was wearing a black wool lined robe and lined trousers. There were several knife wounds on the head, and it was definitely killed by hacking. Photographs were taken and the body was sent to the morgue for storage, pending the arrest of the perpetrators. However, some bystanders said that the deceased was in love with a seventeen-year-old girl, but the girl had another lover. The triangular love affair led to the grisly murder. However, they claimed not to know the names and kept the content a secret, only sighing and leaving.

Verdict in the Case of Mixing Spun Yarn with Enemy Goods 156

Zheng Kang Sentenced to Two Months Imprisonment and a Fine of One Hundred Yuan

Zheng Kang from Ningbo opened the Dafeng Cotton Yarn Shop on Xinxin Bridge Street in the French Concession. Last year, he disguised spun yarn with enemy goods and mixed it with the "Zhong" brand yarn from the Shenxin Spinning Factory. After Shenxin discovered this, they reported it to the police, who sent detectives to seize 43 bales of stolen yarn and took Zheng into custody. He was sent to the Second Special Court for interrogation and sentenced to eight months imprisonment and a fine of three hundred yuan. Zheng refused to accept the verdict and hired lawyer Gu Jirong to file an appeal. The Criminal Court President Wang Gangxu, along with two judges, Li Changnian and Xiong Yinping, held a joint court session and announced the end of the debate. They ordered Zheng to pay a deposit of five hundred yuan as bail, pending the scheduled pronouncement of the verdict. Details have been recorded in the previous newspaper. Yesterday was the day of the verdict. In the afternoon, at 3:00 PM, President Wang, along with the two judges, Li and Xiong, arrived at the Second Criminal Court and summoned Zheng to court. The judgment was announced, stating that the original verdict was revoked. Zheng Kang's attempt to obtain illegal property benefits through fraud was sentenced to two months imprisonment and a fine of one hundred yuan. If the fine is not paid, he will be supervised in prison, with two yuan equivalent to one day. The number of days of detention before the judgment is determined will be converted to one day of imprisonment for every two days, or one day to two yuan. The 43 bales of cotton yarn are confiscated. Zheng Kang will remain on his original bail.

Trial Opens for Rent Exemption Case in Tongchunfang 157

No Hope for Reconciliation in this Case

Verdict Scheduled for the 26th

Since the Japanese army began attacking Zhabei on January 28th, the battle spread to Shanghai after the 19th Route Army stood up in resistance. All industries came to a standstill, and the citizens suffered heavy losses. Although the ceasefire and troop withdrawal have taken place, the prosperity of Shanghai has not been immediately restored. Due to economic exhaustion after the war, citizens have launched a movement to reduce or exempt rent during the war, in order to ease the burden slightly. The Citywide Rent Reduction and Exemption Committee decided on the methods of reduction and exemption based on the severity of the damage and submitted them to the Municipal Government and the Social Affairs Bureau for assistance. On the landlord's side, those who deeply understood the situation voluntarily reduced rent for two, three, or four months, but those who were unwilling to compromise at all were quite numerous. For example, the landlord of Tongchunfang in North Haining Road, China Land Company, was unwilling to reduce rent because the area was far from the war zone. However, its tenants requested that the rent for February and March be completely exempted according to the decision of the Rent Reduction and Exemption Committee. The opinions of both sides clashed, and reconciliation was unsuccessful. Although the tenants paid the rent arrears up to January first, the landlord's broker, the British company Ewo, was still unwilling to accept it immediately. Pan Shidun, Wu Linkun, and Chen Zhongyin, three lawyers, filed a lawsuit against 17 tenants, including Yongkanghao, for rent arrears. All foreign business owners in this city are paying close attention to this lawsuit. The outcome of this case will determine their standard for dealing with tenants' requests for rent exemption in various unresolved rent issues. Yesterday, Magistrate Lou of the First Special District Court opened the trial. Most of the defendants appeared in court together. Eleven of them jointly hired Yue Junying as their lawyer. First, the plaintiff's lawyer stated the amount of rent owed by each defendant. Then, he stated that Tongchunfang was located in the central district and was not affected by the war at all. Moreover, the businesses operated by the defendants, such as hotels, restaurants, cigarette paper shops, and pharmacies, made three times as much profit during the war. According to the工部局's regulations on wartime tax reduction and exemption, all of the central and western districts are not exempt, which shows that the central district is indeed a safe place and there is no reason to exempt rent. All foreign commercial property groups are now watching the outcome of this case, as a trial run for the judgment. As the rent reduction movement committee is a private organization, the plaintiff absolutely objects to the defendants' request to reduce or exempt rent based on this organization. Finally, he recited the letter from the Rent Reduction Committee to the plaintiff's lawyer and strongly criticized the wording in the letter. Then, the defendant's representative, lawyer Yue, stated that the letter was issued by another organization and was not relevant to this case. Then, he admitted that there was no error in the amount of unpaid rent claimed by the plaintiff. However, he said that the rent should be divided into three periods. The period before January 28th was the first period. The defendants had long wanted to pay the rent during this period, but the plaintiff refused to accept it, so it was deposited in this lawyer's office and is still with the case. Please ask the plaintiff to verify and accept it. February and March are the second period. At this time, Japanese soldiers invaded the territory, and cannons were fired continuously. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce announced a strike to resist the enemy, and the shops could not operate. How could they have the financial resources to pay rent? According to the Civil Code and precedents, if the leased property cannot be used due to force majeure, there is the right to request rent exemption. From April onwards, it is the second period. The property in this case was only transferred to the current owner in July of last year. At that time, the plaintiff verbally allowed the tenants to follow the previous custom that lawsuits would not be filed for rent arrears of less than three months. Therefore, even if it is decided in the future that the rent for February, March, etc. cannot be exempted, it is still not time to pay it, and the plaintiff should not file a lawsuit. The plaintiff's lawyer responded to each point of lawyer Yue's defense. The two sides argued back and forth endlessly. Magistrate Lou persuaded both parties to compromise, abandon the law, and reconcile, because the case was caused by the Sino-Japanese War and not only one industry was affected. However, the opinions of both sides could not be reconciled, and reconciliation was hopeless. Then, the defendant's lawyer paid the rent for January that the defendant had brought to the court to the plaintiff for acceptance and the plaintiff's lawyer revised the amount of the lawsuit. Then, Magistrate Lou announced that the verdict would be pronounced at 2:00 PM on May 26th.

Shoemaker Beats Butcher to Death 161

Zhang Ruichun, 41 years old from Jiangyin, lived at No. 10 Renjin Lane, Yuezhou Road. He had a cooked meat stall at Hongkou Triangle Market. There was a shoemaker from Jiangbei who had a shoemaker's stall nearby for years, and they were both acquaintances. Two months ago, the shoemaker had purchased five intestines from Zhang on credit, totaling 100 cash, which he had not yet paid back. Later, Ruichun had asked him for it once. A few days ago, Zhang brought old shoes to the shoemaker for repair, but he did not pay for the repairs at the time. Yesterday, the two met on the side of the vegetable market, and the shoemaker immediately asked Zhang for the repair fee. Zhang also replied by asking for the money owed for the pig intestines, which led to an argument, followed by violence. The shoemaker happened to have a carrying pole in his hand, and he struck Zhang's chest with the pole, injuring his internal organs. Zhang vomited bright red blood on the spot and fainted. The police officers who heard the news rushed to the scene, detained the shoemaker and sent him to the police station for questioning. The injured man was sent to the Tongren Hospital for treatment, but he died at around 5:00 PM.

Out-of-Work Foreman Threatens Iron Shop Owner 162

Extorting $2,000

Sentenced to Three Years Imprisonment

Wang Piji, the owner of the Wang Jusen Iron Shop at No. 9 Jingshou Lane, Wuhu Road, suddenly received threatening letters starting on the 5th of this month, intending to extort $2,000. The letters contained threatening words, saying that if he did not comply, he would be kidnapped, and the ransom would then increase to $30,000. Wang ignored the letters at first. However, the gang continued to send letters, reaching six in total. Wang then reported the letters to the police station for investigation. On the 18th, Wang received a seventh letter, asking to meet at 2:00 PM the day before yesterday in a deserted area next to the Xujiahui Railway. The person who came was to put the money in a cigarette paper box under the coffin, but the amount gradually decreased from $2,000 to $200. Wang then reported to the Old Gate Police Station, and sent Detective Chief Hole, Chinese Detective Lang Zuyin, and Chinese Detective Bao Yusi to go to Xujiahui with Wang Piji. They put a cigarette box under the coffin and then dispersed and ambushed. Before long, a Shanghai gang member, Shen Licang, arrived and wandered around the area for a long time, for about an hour. The Chinese and foreign detectives, seeing his suspicious behavior, stepped forward to arrest him and took him and the cigarette box back to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Criminal Court One of the First Special District Court. According to the police lawyer Ru Baoyi's statement of the case, and submitting the seven threatening letters as evidence, and according to the plaintiff Wang Piji's complaint of the previous situation, when questioned, the defendant confessed that he was a foreman at the plaintiff's shop three years ago, and now he is in extreme poverty, so he resorted to this tactic. All seven threatening letters were written by him alone. After investigation, President Qian Hongye sentenced the defendant Shen Licang to three years imprisonment and confiscated the seven threatening letters.

Continued Trial of the Case of the Six-Year-Old Girl's Tragic Death 167

Awaiting Forensic Examination for Further Review

Zhong Yuehua, a 15-year-old from Jiangbei, was an apprentice at the Qin tailor shop at No. 1047 Yongxiang Lane, Donghanbili Road. On the morning of the 25th of last month, at 11:00 AM, she was chopping wood at the back door when Zhou Gendi, a six-year-old girl from Shaoxing, a neighbor, was harassing her. Zhong angrily struck the girl's private parts with the axe handle. The Jiuxing Road Police Station was notified and sent Detective Zhou Kaiwen to take Zhong into custody and send her to the First Special District Court. Details have been reported in this newspaper. During the postponement, the girl's condition worsened at the Guangren Hospital, and she died at 11:50 AM on the 17th. The body was sent to Fielun Road for examination. Zhong was punished by the court. Yesterday morning, Judge Shen Bingrong held a trial at Gao Yi Court. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin stated the previous situation and said that the Guangren Hospital doctor examined the body and found that the girl Zhou Gendi's vaginal bone was broken, which was fatal, and there were X-ray photos to prove it, but it was slightly different from the examination by the court's forensic doctor. The photos were presented for inspection. The court ordered forensic doctor Wei, who had examined the case, to come to the court. The X-ray photos were given to Wei for review. After examining the photos, forensic doctor Wei said that the girl's private parts had been swollen for a long time, and the swelling had subsided. The X-ray photos were presented in court for study during the trial, etc. According to the girl's mother, Zhou Zhu, she told the defendant that if the injury was serious, she would be severely investigated, and she also told the owner of the tailor shop about the matter. She only had this daughter and asked for justice. When questioned, Zhong Yuehua denied hitting the girl's private parts with the axe handle, saying that she fell on her own. She hired lawyer Fan Gang to defend her. Judge Shen ordered her to be remanded in custody, pending forensic doctor Wei's appraisal and further verification from the Qin tailor shop owner.

Chinese Thrift and Virtue Society Strives to Re-establish 172

The Chinese Thrift and Virtue Society was originally a pure public organization formed by Chinese people. For over a decade, it has enjoyed an outstanding reputation. Since Wang Chengdian assumed the position of Director-General, he has devoted himself even more to social endeavors, achieving remarkable results. During the recent Shanghai Incident, the society was unfortunately in the direct line of fire, and its premises were occupied by the Japanese military. The details of these events were reported in various newspapers at the time. Subsequent investigations revealed that while the society's building still stands, the internal losses were substantial. Most of the historical documents and important ledgers from previous years have been scattered and lost. It is now reported that the society's board of directors and committee members, in light of the current societal extravagance, believe that the society, with its duty to correct social customs, should restore its original state as soon as possible to maintain public welfare and seek the well-being of its members. In addition to having already reported to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau for record-keeping, they are currently undertaking reorganization, and it is expected that the society will soon regain its former appearance.

Weather Report 174

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the coastal areas of Shandong province are mostly cloudy with southwesterly winds. The Yangtze River basin and the coastal areas here are overcast and showing signs of change, with possible thunderstorms and moderate cyclones caused by a small low-pressure system moving in a northeasterly direction. Heavy fog is present along the coast south of Ma'an Island, and wind conditions are unstable. Furthermore, in the 24 hours preceding 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in the city was 84.7 degrees and the lowest was 66.2 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest temperature was 7.0.5 degrees and the lowest was 55.0 degrees.

Education News

Important News

Drafted by the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education 176

Three-Year Education Plan (1) 177

Education in Jiangsu Province in recent years has been hampered by financial difficulties, preventing progress. Furthermore, those administering education have often treated it merely as a means of livelihood, perfunctorily fulfilling their duties. Administrative organs have been constantly besieged, preoccupied with dealing with requests for funds, and have lost their function of supervising and promoting education. Since Zhou Fo-hai assumed the position of Director, he has achieved some success in managing provincial education funds and rectifying local education. Now, there is a proposal for a three-year plan. Here is a summary of the draft.

First Goal 178

The goal of this plan is to achieve the following effects within a short period of three years: (1) increase enrollment opportunities for school-age children, reducing the number of children out of school by 5% each year; (2) increase literacy opportunities for illiterate adults, reducing the number of illiterate people by 10% each year; (3) ensure that students graduating from schools who wish to serve society possess sound service abilities and the qualities expected of a citizen; (4) ensure that graduating students who wish to pursue further education have the academic ability to do so.

Second Content 179

To increase enrollment opportunities for school-age children, universal education should be actively promoted. To truly universalize compulsory education, the training of teachers is a prerequisite. To ensure that graduating students have sound service abilities, the content of vocational schools should be enriched. To reduce the number of illiterate people year by year, the implementation of literacy education should be strengthened. To ensure that graduates have the ability to pursue further education, the level of secondary education should be improved. Therefore, (1) universalizing compulsory education, (2) expanding normal schools, (3) enriching vocational education, (4) raising the level of secondary education, and (5) promoting literacy education are the central tasks of this plan.

Third Basis 180

The educational funds of Jiangsu Province, in terms of education, include the busy canal surtax, slaughter tax, and various other taxes, with an annual revenue of approximately 2.8 million yuan. Furthermore, the funding for National Central University has already been transferred to the central government this year. If the assessed amount can be collected in full, then specialized education, vocational education, normal education, and social education can be enriched and developed. As for local education, the total educational expenses of all counties in the province have reached over 12 million yuan. Although the actual collection amount in the autumn audit each year often differs from the assessed amount, if we calculate based on the actual collection amount averaging over 60%, then it should be at least over 7.5 million yuan annually. In terms of educational institutions, the province has 21 middle schools, 16 normal departments, 2 specialized schools, 6 rural normal schools, 15 experimental primary schools, and 4 vocational schools. In the counties, there are over 70 middle schools, 48 normal schools, and a total of 13,756 grades in primary schools, with approximately 580,000 students enrolled. The number of children out of school is still around 3,995,296. As for illiterate people, there are 25 million, accounting for nearly 80% of the population of 32 million. However, overall, the current state of education in Jiangsu Province is showing signs of exhaustion. The reasons for this can be summarized as two points: (1) The province's and local finances have long suffered from the problem of nominal revenue exceeding actual expenditure, and there has been no effective rectification. The extravagance and disorder of local finances are even more difficult to address. Furthermore, disasters and warfare have repeatedly occurred, leading to the accumulation of huge debts in provincial and county finances, making auditing difficult and resource extraction impossible. Maintaining the status quo is already difficult, let alone expanding. This is due to the lack of development caused by financial difficulties. (2) Because local finances have accumulated excessive debts, educational personnel feel insecure. In addition, factions are divided, each establishing its own camp, engaging in mutual attacks and exclusion, both overt and covert. As a result, lawsuits against bureau chiefs, encirclements of education bureaus, assaults on bureau members, and strikes for salary have become common practice. The chaos in local education is on the verge of being irreparable. This is due to personnel disputes that have led to the increasing deterioration of local education. Given the current state of education in Jiangsu Province, any practical plan should rigorously rectify what needs to be rectified and strive to expand what urgently needs to be developed. Therefore, the implementation of this plan must be divided into specific steps.

Fourth Steps 181

The current state of education in Jiangsu Province shows signs of exhaustion. If it is not thoroughly rectified from all aspects, the foundation cannot be stabilized. Without a solid foundation, talk of progress will only lead to confusion and ineffectiveness. Therefore, thorough rectification must be carried out first, and then gradual expansion should be planned within the possible scope of the current provincial and local economy. Therefore, the implementation steps of this plan are set as: the first year will be the rectification period, and the second and third years will be the expansion period.

First Year: Rectification Period 182

During the implementation of the rectification plan in this period, in order to thoroughly rectify from all aspects, the Department of Education has already formulated "Measures for Evaluating County Magistrates' Education Management Performance" and "Regulations for Evaluating Education Bureau Directors" to assess educational administrators, promulgated "Regulations for Managing Budgeting of County Education Funds" to eliminate the problem of nominal revenue exceeding actual expenditure, revised the "Regulations for the Organization of Education Bureaus" to save administrative expenses, conducted special inspections to thoroughly address the education in counties with the most disputes, and divided old debts from new revenues to determine a method for repaying old debts in order to facilitate the progress of education. Furthermore, strict orders have been issued to all county education bureaus to eliminate extravagant spending, and education bureaus with uncleared accounts have been given deadlines to expedite the clearing of accounts. In addition to the above, the following items should be implemented:

1. Rectify various sources of funding

(A) Negotiate methods of coordinated collection. County treasuries have become accustomed to fraudulent collection practices. Therefore, it is necessary to negotiate with the Department of Finance to determine appropriate methods of coordinated collection to prevent treasuries from concealing and delaying payments.

(B) Rectify school land, school rent, education surtaxes, and slaughter taxes. The problems with school land and school rent in various counties are also deep-rooted and urgently need thorough rectification, as well as a reasonable increase in rent. There is also room for rectifying and increasing education surtaxes. If the slaughter taxes in the province can be further rectified, there is still potential for an increase. The revenue from the three items of rectification and increase should be used to enrich the content of compulsory education and social education in various counties.

2. Increase the number of students in each grade of primary schools throughout the province

The total number of primary schools in Jiangsu Province is 8,199, with 23,756 grades. The average number of students per grade is approximately 40. Each grade should be increased to 50 students. Based on the original number of grades, this year alone, an additional 137,560 school-age children can be enrolled.

3. Improve primary school teaching methods

Local primary schools should be urged to study multi-grade teaching and single-grade teaching, and efforts should be made to organize workshops or encourage correspondence schools.

4. Improve private schools

Although the enrollment rate of children in the province is over 14%, the number of children attending private schools should not be less than 10%. Therefore, at a time when compulsory education funds are not yet sufficient, improving private schools is a crucial task. Private school registration, private school teacher registration, and private school teacher certification should be implemented to achieve the goal of transforming private schools into formal schools.

5. Rectify the academic atmosphere

Correct the frivolous and romantic tendencies and cultivate a pure and studious atmosphere.

6. Actively improve normal education

There are only 16 normal departments in provincial middle schools, 6 provincial rural normal schools, and 43 county normal schools in the province. The total number of graduates from provincial and county schools each year is approximately 1,700. However, there are already many who pursue further education or switch to other occupations. Even if all of them could serve in primary schools, assuming one teacher per grade, this number of 1,700 would be significantly insufficient to cover the 13,756 grades. Therefore, during this period, in addition to the Department of Education continuing to implement primary school teacher certification to provide relief, the improvement plan for normal education includes three items: (A) implementing the independence of rural normal schools, (B) gradually implementing the independence of normal middle schools, and (C) establishing normal specialized schools.

Education Funds for the 21st Year

The previous year's budget was over 2.73 million yuan

Hangzhou dispatch: The organizational charter of the Zhejiang Provincial Budget Committee has been approved by the provincial government. The committee members consist of all provincial committee members, the Secretary-General, the President of the High Court, and the Director of the Security Bureau. Zhou Junyan, Director of the Department of Finance, and Lu Dai, the Secretary-General, were elected as standing committee members. The first review meeting was held at the Department of Finance at 2:00 PM on the 18th. The budget committee members present included Zhou Junyan, Yang Mianzhong, Chen Bulei, Wang Chengying, and Lu Dai.
