The result is still good. If all provincial institutions can follow suit and seriously reduce expenses, the income and expenditure can be expected to balance.

General Situation of National People's School Education 184

Records of Striking the Bell at an Ancient Temple (1): Not Removing the Weeds in the Courtyard of the Village School Teacher 185

"Records of Striking the Bell at an Ancient Temple" is a notebook written casually by a bell-striking worker, not a systematic work. In it, you can see how he integrates his own life with the lives of everyone in the village, big and small, depicting the movements deep in their hearts. You can say it is his autobiography, or you can say it is a living history of a small society. Society is the school, and living is education. Then you can say it is a portrait of a school or a small shadow of education. This text is written with ant-like small characters on the bell he strikes, from the inside to the outside, from the bottom to the top, covering the entire bell weighing 108,000 jin. The bell-striker did not leave his name because his job is striking the bell. When he was young, people called him Bell-Boy; when he grew up, people called him Mr. Bell. He silently accepted this title. His notebook also has content but no title. Please allow me to title it "Records of Striking the Bell at an Ancient Temple" and introduce it to everyone.

(1)

Everyone says that the temple where I live is the oldest temple in the world, but when asked which dynasty it was built in, no one in the village can answer. The annual rings of the two pine trees in front of the temple tell people that they have stood there for 1,500 years. However, it would be too arbitrary to assume that the age of this ancient temple is the same as the size of the pine trees. But the people in our village do not have the time to study these things. What they still say is, "The oldest temple in the world!" If there are guests, they always proudly point to the ancient temple and say, "This is the oldest temple in the world!" Once, a tourist came and, hearing this boast, told the guide, "Humanity has existed for a million years, and before humans, the earth exploded from the sun 200 million years ago. Before the earth, the arrangement of stars in the entire universe had already existed for billions of years. What is your few thousand-year-old temple?" Although his words were reasonable, we could not refute him at the time. But afterwards, we thought that we also had reasons to defend the ancient temple. This temple is older than any house in the village. The oldest old men in the village say that their grandmothers and great-grandmothers had made wishes and burned incense here. Indeed, this ancient temple has witnessed the fall of the Han people twice and twice taken China back from the hands of others.

Zhejiang and Shanxi Provinces Opened the Earliest

The Ministry of Education has investigated and compiled statistics on the teaching affairs of citizen schools in various provinces and cities. The important matters are extracted below.

(1) Regarding the opening of citizen schools, Zhejiang and Shanxi provinces were the earliest (in 1919), while Yunnan, Ningxia, and Weihaiwei were the latest (in 1931). Two districts were opened in each of the years 1924 and 1925, four districts in 1927, two districts in 1928, six districts in 1929, and one district in 1930. (2) Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Jiangxi, Henan, Shaanxi, Sichuan, Shanghai, and other seven provinces and cities have established ordinary citizen schools and also set up advanced citizen schools or advanced classes. Yunnan is planning to set up advanced citizen schools. The remaining fourteen provinces and cities only have ordinary citizen schools. (3) Only Gansu province has full-time teaching staff, while the rest are part-time. Their qualifications are mostly secondary school graduates, with a small number of social education agency personnel serving part-time. (4) Teachers' salaries: Yunnan province is purely voluntary. Shandong is the highest, with monthly salaries ranging from 20 to 50 yuan. Hubei's full-time teachers receive 45 yuan per month, Ningxia 20 to 40 yuan, Sichuan and Weihaiwei 4 yuan each. In addition, four provinces offer less than 10 yuan per month, one province 6 to 16 yuan, two provinces 10 yuan, three provinces 12 yuan, one province 15 yuan, one province 6 to 40 yuan, and four provinces 20 yuan. (5) Sichuan province adopts a system of separate classes for boys and girls, Henan has separate schools for boys and girls, and the rest are co-educational. The largest percentage of boys is in Rehe, accounting for 98%, and Shandong 95.2%. The smallest percentage is in Shanghai, accounting for 44%. The largest percentage of girls is in Shanghai, accounting for 56%. The smallest percentage is in Shandong, accounting for 4.8%, and Rehe 2%. (6) The lowest age of students is 8 years old, and the highest is 61 years old. Rehe is 8 to 49 years old, Hubei 10 to 20, Beiping 10 to 30, Nanjing 10 to 50, Gansu 12 to 30, Jiangnan 12 to 32, Guangdong and Shaanxi both 12 to 46, Anhui 12 to 43, Shandong, Qingdao, and Chahar all 12 to 45, Zhejiang and Ningxia 12 to 50, Weihaiwei 12 to 48, Shanghai 12 to 56, Sichuan 13 to 56, Jiangsu 14 to 50, Henan 14 to 61, Shanxi and Suiyuan 15 to 38, and Yunnan 16 to 40. (7) Three districts have a study period of three months, fifteen districts four months, one district three to six months, one district four to six months, and six months and one year each in one district. Regarding opinions on the length of the study period, four months is the basic principle. Five districts advocate not extending it, one district advocates extending it by half a month, four districts by one month, and three districts by two months. In reality, one district has already increased it by two months and one district by eight months.

Local News

Municipal Bureau of Education Announces Revised Regulations for Supplementary Schools and Worker Supplementary Schools 186

The Regulations for the Appointment and Dismissal of Teaching Staff of Shanghai Municipal Worker Supplementary Schools and the Detailed Rules of Service for Teaching Staff of Shanghai Municipal Worker Supplementary Schools were previously formulated by the Municipal Bureau of Education in 1928 and submitted to the Municipal Government for promulgation and implementation. Now, the bureau considers that the supplementary schools have been changed to a central system, and the previous regulations are not very applicable. Furthermore, because the regulations for the appointment, dismissal, and service of teaching staff are interrelated, they have been revised and consolidated into the Regulations for the Appointment, Dismissal, and Service of Principals, Directors, and Teaching Staff of Shanghai Municipal Supplementary Schools. The original Article 3 of the Simplified Rules for Shanghai Municipal Worker Supplementary Schools has also been revised. All have been submitted to the Municipal Government for approval, and the Ministry of Education has been notified for record and promulgation.

Revised Regulations for the Appointment, Dismissal, and Service of Principals, Directors, and Teaching Staff of Shanghai Municipal Supplementary Schools (Approved and promulgated by the Municipal Government on May 14, 1932, approved by the Ministry of Education for record)

Article 1: Each central supplementary school shall have one principal, and other supplementary schools shall have one director. They shall administer the entire school's administration in accordance with the educational policy of the National Government and various relevant educational laws and regulations. The principal shall also administer the administration of each school within the central school district. Article 2: The principals and directors of each school shall be appointed by the Municipal Bureau of Education, and the teaching staff shall be hired by the principals or directors and reported to the Municipal Bureau of Education for record. Article 3: Anyone with one of the following qualifications may serve as a principal, director, or teacher in a supplementary school: (1) Those with the qualifications of teaching staff in municipal primary schools in this city. (2) Those who have graduated from vocational schools and have educational experience. Article 4: The term of office for principals, directors, and teaching staff of each school shall be one year. However, those who have achieved significant results may be continuously appointed. Article 5: If the principals, directors, or teaching staff of supplementary schools commit one of the following acts and are confirmed by the Bureau of Education, their duties may be suspended at any time: (1) Violating the party principles of the Chinese Kuomintang. (2) Violating the educational policy of the National Government and various relevant educational laws and regulations. (3) Ineffective school management and inability to improve. (4) Unethical conduct and embezzlement of school funds. (5) Immoral behavior and degraded character. (6) Physical or mental defects that prevent the performance of duties. Article 6: The duties of the principals, directors, and teaching staff of each school are stipulated as follows: A. Principals and Directors: (1) Implement the Three People's Principles education. (2) Handle all internal and external affairs. (3) Examine the service performance of teaching staff and promote or dismiss teachers with the approval of the Municipal Bureau of Education. (4) Supervise teaching staff in handling student admissions, withdrawals, attendance, absences, etc., and prepare various forms and registers. (5) Manage school property and finances, and prepare budget estimates and final accounts, which shall be submitted to the Municipal Bureau of Education for review. (6) Assess student performance and issue graduation certificates. The principals of each central school shall also be responsible for examining the service performance of the directors of each school within the central district and guiding the directors of each school to unify and improve teaching and management. B. Teaching Staff: (1) Pay attention to improving the teaching methods of the subject taught. (2) Examine the personality of students, provide appropriate cultivation, and examine the learning process inside and outside the classroom to provide guidance. (3) Assess students' academic performance, character, and behavior. (4) With the approval of the principal or director, investigate the reasons for students' absences and withdrawals, and contact their service organizations or families to persuade them to return. (5) Prepare various forms and registers. (6) Handle matters entrusted by the principal or director and various meetings. Article 7: If the principal or director of each school needs to take leave for more than three days, he/she should appoint a person to be responsible for the duties and submit it to the Municipal Bureau of Education for approval. If teaching staff need to take leave, they should report to the principal or director and appoint a person to take over the duties. Article 8: The principal or director of each school may concurrently serve in school affairs. Article 9: These regulations shall be implemented from the date of approval by the Municipal Government.

Simplified Rules for Shanghai Municipal Worker Supplementary Schools (Approved and promulgated by the Municipal Government on January 17, 1929, approved by the Ministry of Education for record on May 14, 1932)

Article 1: The Bureau establishes several worker supplementary schools to improve workers' knowledge, increase work efficiency, and cultivate their character. Article 2: The standard class size for each school is 30 to 50 students. Article 3: Each school shall admit workers aged 15 or above who have some literacy skills. Article 4: Students should invite a guarantor to come to the school to fill out a guarantee form upon admission. Article 5: Each school's curriculum is divided into the following subjects: Party Principles, National Language, National Common Sense, Service Morality, Industrial and Commercial Common Sense, Practical Correspondence, Written Calculation, Abacus Calculation, Overview of Various Industries, Simple Bookkeeping, Simple English, and vocational lectures and vocational guidance are held from time to time. Article 6: Each school has 100 minutes of class per day. The class time should not interfere with the workers' off-campus work. Article 7: All students of each school are free of charge. Article 8: The study period for students of each school is one year, and the graduation period is determined based on the complexity of the subjects and the level of the students. Article 9: These simplified rules shall be implemented from the date of promulgation by the Municipal Government.

Bao Shan Education Bureau Strives to Restore Education 187

Transferring 15,000 Yuan from the Relief Association

To Prepare for Selective Repairs and Sustain Education

During the Songhu Battle, Baoshan bore the brunt and the entire territory was occupied. Cultural institutions, being objects of enemy aversion, were especially devastated. Now that the enemy has retreated and the territory is being reclaimed, efforts should be made to restore them. Pu Wengui, the director of the county's education bureau, sent a special letter to the War Relief Association yesterday, requesting a loan of 15,000 yuan to facilitate selective repairs and procurement, so as to restore the original state as soon as possible. The letter is recorded below:

Letter to the Relief Association: Respectfully, during the Songhu Battle, our county bore the brunt, and the educational institutions suffered heavy losses. Subsequently, due to the retreat of our troops to the rear defense, the entire territory was occupied, and the cultural institutions were further devastated due to enemy aversion, destroyed almost completely. Once detailed investigations are completed, we will report and request funding for relief. Although the ceasefire and troop withdrawal have occurred, the wounds are deep and restoration to the original state is extremely difficult. The county's education budget averages over 10,000 yuan per month, with 70-80% coming from land taxes. Last year's poor harvest due to floods forced us to borrow to survive, which was already difficult to sustain. The impact of this war has halted tax collection, and with the exemption of urgent grain transport, there is no source of income, leading to financial exhaustion and a desperate situation. How to raise regular funding in the future has already been reported to the provincial authorities for approval, along with a request for an advance allocation of 15,000 yuan for temporary losses for various schools, to facilitate selective repairs and procurement, so as to restore the original state as soon as possible. To date, there has been no approval. With resources running out, coping is difficult. Therefore, we specifically request that your association, considering the importance of local education and the potential for school children in the disaster area to be deprived of education, find a way to transfer a loan of 15,000 silver yuan from the relief funds received by the county. Once the provincial funds are claimed, or when the county's share of education relief funds is obtained, the loan will be repaid as soon as possible, in order to address both needs and sustain education. We would be endlessly grateful. Addressed to the Baoshan War Relief Association, Director Pu Wengui.

Report to the Provincial Education Department: Report concerning the request to instruct the War Relief Association to approve the allocation of school loss funds. The Shanghai Incident occurred, and this county was forced into the intense firing line, causing significant damage to various educational institutions. Subsequently, due to the retreat of our troops, the entire territory fell into the hands of the Japanese army, and cultural institutions were further devastated due to enemy aversion, destroyed almost completely. Once the military situation settles, a detailed investigation will be conducted and reported. This unprecedented catastrophe is heartbreaking to contemplate. Although a ceasefire agreement has been reached and troop withdrawal is imminent, restoring the original state is extremely difficult. The county's education budget averages over 10,000 yuan per month, with 70-80% coming from land taxes. Last year's poor harvest due to floods forced us to borrow to survive, as reported in previous submissions. The occurrence of this war has halted tax collection, and with the exemption of urgent grain transport, there is no source of income, leading to financial exhaustion and a desperate situation. How to raise regular funding in the future is a matter to be decided. We request that you, sir, consider that local education is vital to the nation, and that school children in the disaster area face the risk of being deprived of education. Please promptly approve and instruct, and also request a report to the provincial government to allocate 15,000 yuan from the war relief funds for the war loss expenses of various schools, to facilitate selective repairs and procurement, so as to restore the original state as soon as possible. We are awaiting your instructions with utmost urgency. Respectfully submitted to the Jiangsu Provincial Education Department, Director of the Baoshan County Education Bureau, Pu Wengui.

A Record of Inspection of the Severely Affected 188

Lida Academy

Total Losses Exceed 140,000 Yuan

丨 Production Education Institutions Should Be Restored Urgently 丨

Lida Academy, being at the epicenter of the Jiangwan War, suffered severe damage. Yesterday, this reporter accompanied the academy's representatives, Mr. Yu Shikuang, Hu Husheng, and Li Zhongming, to inspect the site. The situation observed was extremely tragic. The buildings set on fire and destroyed by the enemy include three teacher and staff dormitories (multi-story buildings) and over fifty large and small chicken coops. Those bombed by enemy aircraft include a girls' dormitory and junior high classrooms (multi-story building), the First Farm Factory, a greenhouse, a teacher's residence, and a breeding chicken farm office. The estimated cost of these destroyed buildings alone is over 50,000 yuan. According to reports from academy representatives Kuang Husheng and others, other losses include over 5,000 volumes of books, over 30 cabinets of instruments, over 300 sets of desks, benches, beds, and over 400 breeding chickens, over 8,000 pounds of honeycomb foundation, over 900 bottles of honey, over 20 boxes of breeding bees, and over 500 boxes of student belongings, with a total value estimated at over 90,000 silver yuan. Moreover, the losses incurred by the Nanxiang branch and the furniture, luggage, and books looted from over ten faculty residences are incalculable. The academy is the most successful promoter of production education in Shanghai, and most of its assets were accumulated through the frugality of teachers and students over the past seven years. The losses suffered are truly regrettable. However, it is heard that the academy's directors, Yi Yincun, Li Shizeng, and Wu Zhihui, are all strongly advocating for restoration, and it is hoped that their efforts will soon be realized.

Business News

Financial and Gold Markets Experience Occasional Turmoil 190

Fifteen Taels of Fluctuations. Yesterday's Gold Price Auction Was Quite Turbulent. The fluctuations were unstoppable, rising and falling a total of fifteen taels. The net decline was only five mace. The market was flat in the morning and unmoved by the fall in the silver market. Afterwards, foreign exchange was nominally flat but effectively strong, and the exchange rate was slightly down. The resolve of the dealers was firm, and the buyers were emboldened, pushing the price straight up to the skies, soaring ten taels, and breaking through the 730 tael mark. At noon, it seemed there were more sellers, and the price immediately declined. Later, there were rumors that Japanese military personnel strongly opposed the Suzuki Cabinet, and with the excessive abundance of foreign exchange, major players excitedly sold off, causing a plunge of ten taels, settling at 715 taels, before returning to a more stable trend. The detailed account of the day is recorded below:

Vigorous in the Morning, Subdued Later. Opening Price for July 191

The opening price for July was still 719 taels and 5 mace. The large silver bars continued to fall by a quarter, and both public and private telegram prices for silver fell by 3/8, but the European market was weak, and there were few sellers. Next, it was 18 taels and 8 mace. Then, Hengyu, Yifeng, Yong Qian, Chang Xiang, Shunli, Hengchang, Yongyu, He, and others entered the market to buy, and the price immediately rose by 5 taels. Furthermore, with the initial settlement price for August US dollars at 31.1875, and only 31 yuan fluctuating slightly, at 9:15, it was 24 taels and 2 mace. Soon after, Tai Chang, Yuan Mao, Yong Zhi, Feng Yong, and others sold, yielding by 2 taels, to 22 taels. When the HSBC exchange rates were announced without change, the price was 22 taels and 7 mace, while internally, it strengthened further. The central bank sold June US dollars at 30.375, and August at 875. The central bank then entered an order, and Qian Chang, Xiang, Yifeng, Yong, Hengchang, Yongyu, He, and others bravely advanced, causing the market price to jump by more than 7 taels, reaching 32 taels and 2 mace at 10:00. The fluctuation was just over one tael every half hour. Afterwards, Xie Xing, Yong Yi Cheng, Bing Xing, and small brokers like Sima Lisi sold off, followed by Wan Xing Shunli. As the US dollar seemed to ease, half a yuan could be settled for June, and HSBC offered 875 for August, which Sumitomo absorbed, causing the gold price to drop sharply by over 3 taels. After 10:30, it was 26 taels and 7 mace, recovering by 2 taels ten minutes later, but after 10:45, it declined again. Hong Kang Yong and most long positions exited, and at 11:10, it was 25 taels and 2 mace. Suddenly, it was rumored that a certain bank was absorbing spot goods, and US and Japanese banks were trading August US dollars at 4375, pulling the price up by 2 taels again, reaching 27 taels and a half at 11:30. But Zhi Feng Yong, Heng Yu, Dalian gangs, etc., came to sell, and with HSBC selling to Sumitomo recent British gold at 9375, the price plunged by 4 taels, reaching 23 taels and 3 mace at noon, then closed at 4 taels and 7 mace. The listed price remained at 793 taels, ranging from 70 taels to 63 taels. The noon closing was 70 taels.

Sharp Decline in the Afternoon, Moderate Closing 192

The market opened in the afternoon at 24 taels, then 24 taels and 8 mace. After 2:15, a strong wind suddenly arose, as there were reports of turmoil in Japanese politics, leading to frequent easing of exchange rates. Various banks sold, with June US dollars initially at 75, then 31.125 for settlement, and Shanghai offering 6875 for September, and HSBC offering 18.1875 for the first order. On the trading floor, Yi Feng, Da De Cheng, Bing Xing, Yuan Da Yong, etc., sold quite a bit, causing the market to fall into a slump, plunging by ten taels, to 15 taels at 3:30. With limited fluctuations in between, Heng Yu, Heng Xing, Yuan Mao Yong, Hong Kang Yong, etc., took the opportunity to enter, and small retail short positions also covered. Moreover, with a wheat company absorbing September US dollars at 31.5 yuan, it pulled up by 4 taels and a half, reaching 19 taels and a half at 4:15, then fell slightly by 1 tael, to 18 taels and a half. Silk, Tea, and Haining Cocoon Prices Affected by Restrictions 206

The highest price for foreign silkworm cocoons is only thirty-five yuan.

Due to the failure of sericulture last year, silkworm farmers in various towns and villages of Haining mostly incubated foreign breeds, and the native breeds left were kept for non-incubation. Unfortunately, the weather was unfavorable, and the new cocoons only yielded slightly more than 30% of the harvest. Very few cocoon firms opened for business. Although the goods arriving on the market these days are not seen to be flourishing, cocoon prices are surprisingly low. The highest price for foreign breed cocoons only opened at thirty-five yuan. Native breed cocoons are not collected, purely affected by the restricted cocoon prices, and the cocoon cost for each dan (unit of weight) for silkworm farmers must pull in fifty-six yuan, resulting in huge losses. Most are taken back for self-drying and reeling to produce native silk for sale. Therefore, the amount collected by various firms is not much.

Ningzhou tea opens at a low price

Since the official opening of Qimen tea trading the day before yesterday, yesterday, firms such as Jardine Matheson, Tientsin Union, Duddell, and Jinlong all started operations. The total transaction volume in the city was more than 1,800 boxes, and the transaction was quite active. However, the firms are still strict with the market prices, and Chinese tea merchants suffer significant losses. Ningzhou black tea, the market also opened yesterday by Duddell at eighty-five taels, which is thirty taels lower than last year. The overall trend of black tea was not considered very optimistic last night. For Su'an Zhenmei green tea, Jinlong, Xiehe, and other firms are keenly interested, but the market price fell to one hundred and thirteen taels, which is fifty to sixty taels lower than before, and tea merchants have no profit to gain.

The Tea Industry in Hekou is Sluggish 208

The town of Hekou in the Gan area has always been known for its thriving tea industry. In recent years, due to the frequent activities of the communists, the Hui merchants have completely lost their capital, causing the tea industry to decline sharply. This year, there are only two tea factories in the area, both established by local merchants. These businesses specialize in black tea. It is heard that due to the sluggish market, the tea price is only around thirty yuan, which is not actually expensive. As for the green tea produced in Huangyuan, Geyuan, Anhua, and other areas, because no foreign firms are taking the lead, they are all being converted into maoqing tea in order to sell through local shops.

Free Talk

Ma Xiangbo, an old man of ninety-three, quotes

Three years ago. Old Master Xiang's ninetieth birthday was being celebrated. Mr. Hu Shi suggested. "There should be two or three secretaries.

Always follow the teacher around. Record his golden words." We wanted to do this "experiment". But the hasty publication. Inevitably there are errors. It should be corrected in the future.

Accomplice 214

—

The old man rests at nine o'clock in the evening. He gets up around four in the morning. During sleep. Never cough. Not to mention spitting phlegm. The day the reporter visited. It was a quarter past seven in the morning. He was already busy with breakfast. He drank coffee soup. A piece of bread. Soaked in the soup. Take it for digestion. He ate and talked, with great interest.

You came really early. I got up a little late today. I didn't get up until a quarter past four. However, there are also three hours since you came.

Very strange. Old people suffer from insomnia. Only I can sleep until dawn. However. Honestly lately. I often hear about the Japanese bullying the Chinese during the day. I am very upset. Sometimes I can't sleep at night. My cultivation is not enough to suppress the hatred in my heart.

Damn Japanese. (Slapping the table) I don't know why the grievances. Must use vicious methods. Harm our innocent people. Damn government. (Slapping the table) This time he dared to sign a ceasefire agreement. Be Japan's "accomplice". I was stimulated like this. I can't sleep. I am ultimately one of the more thoughtful people in China. It has been so since I was a child. My mind is often spinning. So fleeting. Easy to forget.

I went to Shanghai in the winter of 1851 (the first year of Xianfeng). I was only eleven years old at that time. After arriving in Shanghai, I entered Xuhui College. Xuhui College was founded in 1839. When I entered the school, there were forty students. About a year after entering the school. I just started reading foreign texts. At that time. The ancient Chinese books. I have already finished reading everything.

Mrs. Stalin 215

— Te

The wife of the king is called the queen. The president's wife is called the First Lady. Who in this world is not pampered and superior to ordinary people. But the wife of Soviet Russia's Dictator Stalin is an exception. Madam is thirty years old. There are two children. Currently studying at a vocational school in Moscow. It is expected to become an expert in manufacturing man-made silk. Classes are held four days every five days. (The fifth day is a Russian day of rest) Currently in the last year of the third year. There are six students in the same class. Madam is the only female student. Diligent and hardworking. Very respected by the professors. During the holidays, most of the other students hang out in the school's dining halls. Madam always uses the remaining time to handle work outside the duties of the Secretariat. Madam's grade. The results are the best in the whole school. Classmates call it "Lu" to honor it. The school authorities always post their grades. As a model for all levels. And encourage the students to strive for progress. Madam's study at the school is not to enjoy special privileges because of her high position. Occasionally violates school rules. Receive the same treatment as other students. A large black board hangs in the main corridor of the school. The surnames of all students who do not come to school for no reason are marked in the list of absentees. One day Madam's name. Also seen on it. The following note stated that three days were missed during the sixteen-day course. And borrowed two books from the school library. Overdue. Madam is in school. Wearing a coarse cloth jacket. Always concentrating on research in the chemical laboratory. Studying tirelessly. After graduation. Will serve as a responsible executive committee member in the Soviet Russian weaving industry. Or a key technical position. Alas. It is truly admirable that a noble lady can condescend to study. Expect to benefit the country. Those heads of state who indulge themselves with the people's fat and ointment should be ashamed to death.

World Small Chronicles 216

— Sea Guest

A woman who lives with skeletons Miss M.L. Tildesley of England was recently appointed administrator of the human osteology department at the Royal College of Surgeons Museum in London. She spends almost all of her working hours with the bones of dead people. There are a total of 6,000 skeletons and several thousand other types of human bones in the room. Among them are more than 3,000 years old. It is truly rare that a young woman can be in such a gloomy and terrifying environment and still enjoy it. According to her, "The purpose of collecting so many human bones in the Department of Human Osteology is to study the racial peculiarities of all mankind. It is possible to discover that each race has its own characteristics. Among them, there is one of the oldest skeletons, which has been handed down from the earliest Stone Age, which is the most valuable. I hope to get a skeleton of a big Hollywood movie tycoon or a movie star and a financial magnate in the future for my research. That would be interesting."

Camel 217

— Fengji

The "Historical Records of the Huns" mentions the strange animal camel. It is also known as the camel. It is produced in the northwest provinces. And the Outer Mongolian area. Transporting goods all depends on it. Wealthy families. Raising camels is countless. Or transport goods by themselves. Or rent to others. Get a very good profit every year. Camels are cold-resistant and heat-averse. Ugly and strange in shape. Grayish yellow in color. Long neck. The head seems to be looking up. The back is high and raised. Like a saddle. The hooves are huge like cows. In summer, the hair falls out completely. Only the skin and bones remain. That is, drive to the mountains to eat grass. The proverb so-called "putting green" is also. It gradually becomes fat after autumn. Re-enter the pass. In winter, the hair is like a thick blanket. People want to carry. That is, bend the feet to it. If the strength can win, then stand. If you can't win, you won't get up even if you whip it. About 400 pounds can be loaded. More than double the mule.

Camels travel mostly at night. About a hundred miles. When the sun rises, they stay in the store. (There are many camel shops in the north, which are very grand and spacious, and do not house mules and horses.) Because the mountain roads are narrow and dangerous. There are many cars and horses. Afraid of crowding. And avoid the scorching sun. The neck is tied with a copper bell. You can hear the sound two miles away. Each group has more than one hundred heads. There are sixty or seventy heads less. Each camel driver leads twenty heads. Lead with a small lamp. Each goes in order. There is absolutely no mess. It is either up or down. Either fast or slow. As soon as you raise your whip, you respond like a reverberation. There is another chief man. Knows the camel's nature. Good at treating camel diseases. So the maintenance is careful. The husbands all accept his command. But if you are not deeply experienced. Can not fill this role.

Out of Jiayuguan. There is more sand and less water. There are occasional undercurrents. The camel knows the veins of the water. When it encounters it, it stops. Step on the ground with your feet. Dig it and get water. There are also many hot winds. It hurts people and animals very badly. When the wind is coming. The camel knows it. That is, lead the neck and call. Bury the mouth and abdomen in the sand. People always take it as a sign. Support the felt curtain around the four weeks. Enter to avoid its disaster. (Anyone who walks on the grassland must carry a felt curtain. Or make it of coarse cloth. Or make it of felt. There are those who are more than ten feet long.)

In the Gansu and Xinjiang area. Documents are carried by camels. Can be five hundred miles a day. Because the sandy land is open and wide. The pace is large and the speed is fast. Its speed is like wind. Mulan's poem says. The swift camel has a thousand miles of foot. It should not be a false statement.

There is a water bag under the neck. Always store water for backup. People also often take its water to drink. Can withstand hunger. Do not eat or drink for half a month. Walking as usual. Its hair can be used as a mattress. Quite warm. Its skin and bones. It is also a major export.

In the desert area. The path is dangerous. Without camels, there is no way to trade and transport. Communicate with each other. The sky gave birth to this strange animal. There must be a reason.

Science

Candle Manufacturing Method (1) 225

— Yunli

Candles are an important part of our daily necessities, as everyone knows. But do we know the raw materials and methods of manufacturing them? The method of candle manufacturing is very simple. This simple and easy home industry is what our country needs most urgently. So I am here to introduce it.

(1) Method of Selecting Raw Materials

Beef tallow, mutton tallow, palm oil, coconut oil... all can be used to make candles, but the candles made from these oils are not very good. When burning, they either have a foul odor or emit soot. Therefore, in order to avoid these drawbacks, the factories now use paraffin wax and stearin wax to manufacture candles. Because the candles made of these two waxes are not only harder, but also shiny and lovely. When burning, there are no drawbacks such as soot, bad smell, and bending, and the fire is brighter and more durable, so they are quite popular with customers.

(A) Paraffin Wax: Also known as paraffin, this wax is found in both petroleum and wood oil. The method of extraction is to take out the residue after distilling these two oils, add strong sulfuric acid, and the impurities contained in the oil will be completely digested by the strong acid, and the paraffin wax will float on the water, solidify into a solid, and be taken out and washed with clean water to become paraffin wax.

(B) Stearin Wax: Mostly contained in beef tallow and mutton tallow. The method of extraction is to first put water into these two oils, then put them together in a pot and heat them. When the oil is completely melted, add lime milk and simmer over fire. The oil will be transformed by the lime into calcium oleate and calcium stearate, which will condense each other, and a yellow liquid floating on top is stearin wax. The above two materials, made in the United States, are the best, and Mobil Oil Company sells them.

(C) Candlewick: Can be made of very fine cotton yarn. But pay attention, when knitting, it must be soaked in medicine water once, so that the candlewick has alkaline properties. After the candle is extinguished, the candlewick will also be extinguished, so there is no danger of burning into the oil. The candlewick should not be too thick or too thin. If it is too thick, the burning heat will be too high, and the melted wax will not be enough to absorb, resulting in soot, so the candle will not last long. If it is too thin, the melted wax cannot be completely absorbed by the candlewick, and it will flow down from the side of the candle, which is even more uneconomical.

(2) Method of Proportioning Raw Materials

The amount of raw materials for candles must be different according to the different temperatures in spring, summer, autumn, and winter. The temperature in summer is the highest, use eight and a half or nine parts of paraffin, and ten or twelve and a half parts of stearin; the temperature in winter is the lowest, use nine or nine and a half parts of paraffin, and half or one part of stearin; in spring and autumn, the temperature is moderate, use ten or eleven parts of paraffin, and seven or seven and a half parts of stearin. As for the end of spring and the beginning of autumn, the temperatures are different, and the proportioning will also change accordingly. In short, use more stearin when the temperature is high, and use more paraffin when the temperature is low.

The proportioning of the amount is closely related to the quality of the candle. The above proportioning is what I have tested. If readers can test out a better proportioning method, please also publish it in the newspaper for research and to revitalize the industry. Due to space limitations, I will talk about the procedures for making candles tomorrow.

A Corner of Society

Receiving Guests in a Hotel 226

— Hongshui

The ship, which had traveled thousands of miles, was gradually slowing down as it neared its destination. Mr. C, who was traveling in steerage, saw the tall Western-style buildings from across the swaying willow branches on the opposite bank, as well as the wide and flat roads, and the trams and cars that shuttled back and forth... He was silently reciting the beautiful names such as "material civilization," "cultural center," and "the most prosperous area in East Asia."

When the ship was about to dock but had not yet docked at the ×× port, suddenly, with a loud noise, many people wearing coarse cloth short clothes, occasionally mixed with a few people in felt hats and long clothes, rushed from several small boats, desperately fighting to approach the passengers, shouting loudly, "Peace Hotel," "Shenjiang Hotel," "Gaosheng Inn," "..."

Mr. C, who had just come out of the mountains, was examining what was going on when, in an instant, someone was already bending over on his deck chair and suitcase, and pasting a few colorful round pieces of paper like plasters.

"How many pieces of luggage, sir?" The man straightened his waist and said with a smile on his face.

"Four pieces, large and small," Mr. C replied unconsciously; at the same time, the words "×× Hotel, spacious rooms, cheap prices..." printed on the oval paper pasted on the luggage were very clear and tempting to his eyes.

"Okay! Let's get off the boat!" he said, pulling the luggage.

"No, I'm going to take a train to Nanjing right away!"

"That's fine too! Go to the hotel first, wipe your face, wash"

a bit, rest for a while, besides, the train is going to..."

"Ah San, come here!" Then another young man ran over, and the two of them seemed to be "making a fortune," with a kind of victorious light shining in their eyes, and they picked up the luggage and left. Mr. C had no choice but to follow them! As soon as they landed, a horse-drawn carriage, as if it had been waiting for Mr. C for a long time, pulled him up and ran away. In a short while, they arrived at the so-called spacious and clean hotel, which was actually in an alley!

Mr. C did wipe his face, and also drank a glass of soda and ate a meal, and the waiter sent a bill.

The bill is as follows:

Room fee: Three yuan and forty cents

Meal: Fifty-nine cents

Carriage fee (paid on behalf): Two yuan

Porter's tips (paid on behalf): One yuan and sixty cents

Soda: Thirty cents

Police donation: Forty cents

Arts and Entertainment

Riding a Flying Sedan Chair 227

— Xinxiu

The day before yesterday, I visited an old friend, Mr. W. As soon as we met, he said to me, "You came at the right time. I was just about to tell you about my first grand enjoyment in my life! Riding a flying sedan chair." I listened and asked inexplicably, "What? The rich old men in Shanghai only take cars and airplanes. Where did you pick up this new trick? Are you kidding me?"

He said, "No, it's really what people call a flying sedan chair, and the one I rode was a four-person flying sedan chair! The more important and wealthy people are, the less likely they are to be invited to ride it. On the other hand, the ignorant country bumpkins often have the qualifications to ride it. But for me, it was the first time. Although it was a waste of fifteen dollars, I gained some knowledge." His words made me even more confused. I hurried to ask him to explain what was going on.

He then got to the point and said, "The night before last, I passed a road. Several women who made a living by selling their bodies were standing in the oblique wind and drizzle. The light of the light green lamp shone on their powdered faces, making them look even more pale and pitiful. I thought that we are all the same, but they have been working on the street for many years, eating the wind and dew, doing this lowly business. I couldn't help but feel compassion for them and looked at them blankly with pity in my eyes. Who knew they would shout, 'Go! Go for a ride!' Everyone swarmed up, and four people lifted me up from front, back, left, and right, and walked into the alley without my feet touching the ground. I had no choice but to become Zhang Xueliang's comrade and let them do whatever they wanted.

They dragged me into the room and chattered nonsense to me. They were busy with tea, cigarettes, and melon seeds. I refused everything and just closed my eyes, like an old monk in meditation, ignoring them. Suddenly, they started to take off my hat, untie my clothes, and pull off my pants... If I still acted like Comrade Zhang at this time, I would lose my virginity! I have never been to a brothel in my life, and I have guarded myself like jade! I hurriedly resisted with all my strength, and they stopped attacking and said, 'Let's go, let Ah Cai sleep with the young master! It's getting late!' They all went out, leaving only a petite and exquisite woman. The outside of the room was also quiet. I stood up to leave. At first, she looked at me with a lively expression, treating me like a prisoner. Later, seeing that my attitude was firm, she softened and said in a pleading tone, 'Thank you, do a good deed, stay here for one night and help me, so that they won't blame me for not being able to do business, for not being able to keep guests, and for having to suffer. It's like you lost three yuan in mahjong, please spend the night here!' Hearing her say this so pitifully, I gave her five yuan and fled this hell on earth like a fly.

When I came back and checked the ten-yuan bill in my coat, it was gone! I don't know if it was taken away by them or if it fell out when I was pushed and pulled. I didn't care about it. I just considered it the price of fifteen yuan for riding a flying sedan chair once."

I listened and thought silently, why does Shanghai, which claims to be civilized, tolerate these sedan chair carriers, openly on the street, pulling pedestrians to "ride flying sedan chairs" like kidnapping, without prohibiting it?

dismissed. ▲ The case of Zhang Jingqing of Yide Company vs. Shang Wusheng regarding rent arrears (Ruling): The defendant shall repay the plaintiff 37,800 yuan in silver, plus 2,490 taels, 3 mace of silver, with interest at a rate of 5% per annum from April 22 of this year until the date of execution; the litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. ▲ The case of Wu Dongmu Xin vs. Gong Shanghai Second Special District Local Court 230

Civil Judgment ▲ Luo Shuai Shi versus Wang Pinshan and others, debt case (Main text) First defendant Wang Pinshan shall repay the plaintiff one thousand dollars. If unable to repay, second defendant Shen Pingqing shall be liable for substitute repayment. Litigation costs shall be borne by the first defendant. ▲ Ruifeng versus Di Baike, rent arrears and eviction appeal case (Main text) The appeal is rejected. The costs of the second-instance litigation shall be borne by the appellant. ▲ Hefu Real Estate Company versus Zhang Wu Yunqi, breach of contract case (Main text) The defendant shall return the plaintiff's deposit of two thousand taels and pay a penalty of two thousand taels. Litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. ▲ Yongxing Foreign Firm versus Zhenxing Textile Factory, debt case (Main text) The defendant shall pay the original amount of silver five thousand six hundred thirty-nine taels and four mace, plus late payment interest calculated at one percent per month from January 1, 1932 until the date of execution. Litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. ▲ Lu Fei versus Hong Kong Hotel, safe deposit case (Main text) The defendant shall repay the plaintiff's safe deposit of two hundred dollars. Litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. ▲ Da Li versus Qian Youju, rent case (Main text) The defendant shall pay the plaintiff's Mai Li Automobile Company rent of one hundred and fifty-six dollars. Litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. ▲ Wang Telaqi versus Ge Erxu and others, goods payment case (Main text) The defendant Ge Erxu shall pay the plaintiff's goods payment of forty-six dollars and forty-seven cents. The plaintiff's remaining claims are rejected. Litigation costs shall be borne equally by the plaintiff and the defendant Ge Erxu. The first item of this judgment may be provisionally executed. ▲ Fan Wenkui versus Hui Erna, rent arrears case (Main text) The defendant shall pay the plaintiff rent of two hundred and eight taels. Litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. ▲ Di Lai versus Gao Yongqing, goods payment case (Main text) The defendant shall be responsible for clearing and repaying the disputed payment. Litigation costs shall be borne by both parties separately. ▲ Hulin Silk Weaving Co., Ltd. versus Zhou Xiangling and others, commission case (Main text) The retrial appeal is rejected. Retrial litigation costs shall be borne by the retrial plaintiff. ▲ Meifeng National Goods Store versus Yu Tai Qiaji Timber Firm, guarantee debt case (Main text) The defendant shall repay the plaintiff's silver one thousand six hundred eighty-two taels, one mace, eight fen, five li on behalf of Xu Peiqing, plus interest at a rate of five percent per annum from the date of judgment confirmation until the date of execution. Litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. ▲ Gu Baocai versus Si Kui Zi'er, divorce, child custody and return of property case (Main text) The divorce between the plaintiff and the defendant is approved, and the defendant shall hand over their son, Yi Ku Bo'er, to the plaintiff for collection. The defendant's counterclaim is rejected. Litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. ▲ Ao Silanda versus Bao Luochi Weijin and others, loan case (Main text) The defendant Bao Luote Weijin shall repay the plaintiff one hundred and seventy-seven dollars. The defendants Bao Luote Weijin, Mrs. Han Xingkaofu, etc. shall jointly and severally repay the plaintiff one thousand one hundred and fifty dollars, of which the loan of one thousand dollars shall bear interest at one percent per month from October 29, 1931 until the date of execution. The plaintiff's remaining claims are rejected. Litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. ▲ Chen Fukang versus Qi Shunxing, rent arrears and confirmation of lien case (Main text) The defendant shall pay the plaintiff rent of two hundred dollars. The defendant's goods placed in the leased premises are confirmed to be subject to the plaintiff's lien. Litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. ▲ Ji Ermen versus Wu Pinsan, goods payment case (Main text) The defendants shall jointly and severally repay the plaintiff's Maosheng Foreign Firm goods payment of silver seven thousand seven hundred eleven taels, three mace, two fen, warehouse rent of silver twenty taels, war risk insurance of silver one hundred ninety-two taels, one mace, fire insurance of silver sixteen taels, one mace, four fen, transport costs of fifteen taels, and monthly rent of silver fifteen taels from January 5, 1932 until the date of execution, plus fire insurance costs from April 25, 1932 until the date of execution, and annual interest of six percent and five hao from December 5, 1931 until the date of execution. Litigation costs shall be borne jointly and severally by the defendants. ▲ Ye Juyuan and 26 others versus You Zhongshan and others, safe deposit case (Main text) The plaintiff's claim is rejected. Litigation costs shall be borne by the plaintiff. ▲ Siming Bank versus Wang Xingcang, rent case (Main text) The defendant shall pay the plaintiff rent of two hundred and forty dollars. Litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. ▲ Hana Musheng versus Liu Zhongxian and others, loan case (Main text) The defendant Liu Zhongxian shall clear the plaintiff's two hundred dollars. If execution is ineffective, the defendant Jin Wengjia shall clear it on his behalf. Litigation costs shall be borne equally by the defendants. ▲ Xinkang Company versus Yu Xifu, rent arrears and return of property case (Main text) The defendant shall pay the plaintiff rent of two hundred and twenty dollars and return the premises at No. 11, Donglin Lane, Jaxi Road. Litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. The part of the judgment regarding the return of the leased premises may be provisionally executed. ▲ Dong Hengfu versus Ye Yangshi, rent arrears and return of property case (Main text) The defendant shall pay the plaintiff rent of one hundred and sixty-eight dollars. The plaintiff's remaining claims are rejected. The plaintiff shall bear one-quarter of the litigation costs, and the defendant shall bear three-quarters. ▲ Shengjia Sewing Machine Company versus Huizhong Silver Company, objection to execution case (Main text) The plaintiff's claim is rejected. Litigation costs shall be borne by the plaintiff. ▲ Ma Duntang versus Xu Jiufeng and others, rent arrears case (Main text) The defendants Xu Jiufeng and Xu Baotang shall each pay the plaintiff rent of ninety-two dollars. Shen Dansen and Xu Yiqing shall each pay the plaintiff rent of eighty-four dollars. Yuan Houzhi shall pay the plaintiff rent of one hundred and two dollars. Chuan Hongqing and Wu Guowei shall each pay the plaintiff rent of one hundred and twenty-four dollars. Da Li shall pay the plaintiff rent of eighty-eight dollars. Litigation costs shall be borne by the defendants in proportion to the amount of rent owed.

This instruction. ▲ Proclamation For the proclamation of auction, this court is executing the case of creditor Xu Zewei versus debtor She Zheng, also known as She Runzhi, for debt litigation. The debtor's property described below has been sealed and appraised. The auction date is scheduled for 2:00 PM on May 30. The court will send a clerk to direct the executing officer to assist the bailiffs in carrying out the auction. All residents who wish to purchase this property should report to the executing officer's office of this court to register so that they can be led to the location to inspect it before the scheduled purchase date. If there are two or more bidders, the highest bidder will be the purchaser. The full price will be paid on the spot, and the auctioned property will be given to the purchaser for collection. All residents are hereby notified. This proclamation. The details are as follows: 1. Subject of the auction: Movable property (list attached). 2. Location of the property: No. 33, Fengbo Lane, Wusongjiang Road. 3. Minimum price: Three hundred and thirty-three dollars. 4. Location for viewing excerpts: Executing officer's office of this court. 5. Executing clerk: Chen Weihan; Executing officer: Zhang Yushu.
